The Khutbah as a Condition for Jumu'ah
Ruling that Jumu'ah requires two khutbahs before prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the khutbah is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is invalid without two khutbahs before prayer — the khutbah compensates for the missing rak'ahs.

This passage establishes a key condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer: the imam must deliver two khutbahs before the prayer, separated by a brief sitting. The author explains the rationale (compensation for Jumu'ah having two fewer rak'ahs than Dhuhr) and cites the prophetic practice from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the passage and extract the exact condition for Jumu'ah: the imam must deliver two khutbahs before the prayer, with a sitting break between them.
The condition applies to the imam, not the congregation.
2
Understand the rationale
Note the reasoning: Dhuhr has 4 rak'ahs, Jumu'ah has 2 rak'ahs; the two khutbahs substitute for the missing two rak'ahs, making the khutbah a necessary component.
This reasoning is unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith from Ibn 'Umar (Bukhari): the Prophet used to deliver the khutbah standing, then sit, then stand again. This shows the required format.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning (dalala) is clear (qati).
4
Apply the condition
Consider what happens if the khutbah is omitted or defective: since it is a condition (shart), the Jumu'ah prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated as Dhuhr.
This distinguishes it from a sunnah or wajib that can be compensated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۴۹] (۴) ومن شرائطها الخطبة قبل الصلوة يخطب الامام خطبتين يفصل بينهما بقعدة.
(۱) ظہر کی نماز چار رکعتیں ہیں اور جمعہ کی نماز دو رکعتیں ہیں اس لئے دو رکعت کے بدلے میں دو خطبے ہیں۔ اس لئے خطبہ جمعہ کی شرط ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر قال كان النبي الا الله يخطب قائماثم يقعد ثم يقوم كما يفعلون الآن (ه) ( بخارى حاشیہ : (الف) عبداللہ بن عمر سے پوچھا گیا ان گاؤں کے بارے میں جو مکہ اور مدینہ کے درمیان ہیں کہ جمعہ کے بارے میں آپ کی کیا رائے ہے؟ فرمایا ہاں ! اگر ان پر امیر ہوں تو جمعہ قائم کرے (ب ) جب نماز سے فارغ ہوئے تو عمر بن عبدالعزیز نے ان لوگوں سے کہا امام جمعہ قائم کر سکتے ہیں جہاں بھی ہوں (ج ) حضور جمعہ پڑھا کرتے تھے جب سورج ڈھل جاتا تھا (د) حجاج بن یوسف جمعہ کو مؤخر کرتا تو میں، ابراہیم اور سعید بن جبیر تھا تو ان دونوں نے ظہر کی نماز پڑھ لی تھی پھر ہم بات کرتے رہے۔ اس حال میں کہ حجاج خطبہ دے رہا تھا۔ پھر ہم نے اس کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی اور اس کو ہم نے نقل کر لیا (ہ) حضور کھڑے ہو کر خطبہ دیتے پھر بیٹھتے پھر کھڑے ہوتے جیسا آج لوگ کرتے ہیں۔
(4) And among its conditions is the khutbah before the prayer; the imam delivers two khutbahs, separating them by a sitting. ... The Prophet used to deliver the khutbah standing, then sit, then stand again, as they do today.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the khutbah as a condition for Jumu'ah. The author states the condition: the imam must deliver two khutbahs before the prayer, with a sitting between them. The reason given (in Urdu) is that Dhuhr has 4 rak'ahs and Jumu'ah has 2, so the two khutbahs compensate for the missing two rak'ahs. This makes the khutbah a requirement (shart) for Jumu'ah. The proof is from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: the Prophet used to deliver the khutbah standing, then sit, then stand again. This establishes the manner of the khutbah. The commentary also includes additional effects about the ruler's role, though these are more connected to the previous lesson; they are appended in the footnote.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam before Jumu'ah prayer, consisting of two parts with a sitting in between.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Jumu'ah is valid but makruh
B) Jumu'ah is invalid and must be repeated
C) The khutbah can be given after prayer
D) It is acceptable if the congregation agrees

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers the two-part khutbah with a sitting break a condition for Jumu'ah's validity, based on the prophetic practice and the compensation for the shortened prayer.

Time Condition for Jumu'ah Prayer
Ruling with proof on the time condition for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time condition for Jumu'ah prayer, identify the primary dalil (hadith) and secondary evidence (athar), and explain the ruling when the time of Zuhr passes.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah must be prayed in Zuhr time; missing it requires praying Zuhr instead.

This passage establishes one of the key conditions for Jumu'ah prayer: it must be performed within the time of Zuhr. The author provides both a prophetic hadith and an effect from the early Muslims to support this ruling. Understanding this condition is essential to avoid the common mistake of thinking Jumu'ah can be performed at any time on Friday.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The condition being discussed is time. Jumu'ah is valid only within the time of Zuhr. If that time passes, the prayer is invalid.
The ruling is based on the hadith and athar.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites a hadith from Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet prayed Jumu'ah when the sun declined (zawal).
This hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'حين تميل الشمس' (when the sun declines) indicates the start of Zuhr time. Thus Jumu'ah is tied to the time of Zuhr.
The proof is in the timing of the Prophet's practice.
4
Note the secondary evidence
The athar about al-Hajjaj shows that when the governor delayed Jumu'ah, the companions prayed Zuhr first, then prayed with him later and considered that later prayer as supererogatory (nafl).
This confirms that Jumu'ah must be within Zuhr time; otherwise, one must pray Zuhr.
5
Evaluate the practical ruling
If the time of Zuhr passes without performing Jumu'ah, the Jumu'ah is invalid and one must make up Zuhr prayer (qada).
The condition is a condition of validity (shart), not mere recommendation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣٤٨](٣) ومن شرائطها الوقت فتصح فى وقت الظهر ولا تصح بعده. عن انس بن مالك ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي الجمعة حين تميل الشمس. واثر: كان الحجاج يؤخر الجمعة فكنت انا اصلی وابراهيم و سعيد بن جبیر فصليا الظهر ثم نتحدث وهو يخطب ثم نصلى معهم ثم نجعلها نافلة.
And among its conditions is time, so it is valid in the time of Zuhr and not valid after it. From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah used to pray Jumu'ah when the sun declined. And an athar: Al-Hajjaj used to delay Jumu'ah so I and Ibrahim and Sa'id ibn Jubayr would pray Zuhr then talk while he was delivering the khutbah, then we would pray with them and then consider it as supererogatory.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the time condition for Jumu'ah prayer. The author states that one of the conditions of Jumu'ah is that it be performed in the time of Zuhr. If the time of Zuhr passes, Jumu'ah is not valid; instead, one must make up Zuhr prayer. This is supported by a hadith from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet prayed Jumu'ah when the sun declined (zawal), which is the beginning of Zuhr time. Additionally, an effect from the Salaf shows that when the governor al-Hajjaj delayed Jumu'ah beyond its time, the companions prayed Zuhr and then prayed with him later, treating the latter as nafl. This confirms that Jumu'ah must be within Zuhr time.

Key Terms
وقت (waqt): Time as a condition for validity of prayer; specifically the time of Zuhr for Jumu'ah.
اثر (athar): A report from a Companion or Successor, used as secondary proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the time of Zuhr passes without performing Jumu'ah?
A) Jumu'ah should still be prayed
B) One must pray Zuhr instead
C) The prayer is invalid and nothing is required
D) A makeup prayer combining Jumu'ah and Zuhr

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah prayer is valid only within the time of Zuhr; if the time passes, one must pray Zuhr instead.

The Khutbah as a Condition for Jumu'ah
Ruling on khutbah being a condition of Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the khutbah is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah, identify the evidence from the Sunnah and the Companion's statement, and explain the consequence of omitting the khutbah.

Core Idea
Without the khutbah, there is no Jumu'ah — the two khutbahs replace the two missing rak'ahs of Zuhr.

The khutbah before Jumu'ah is not merely a recommended practice; it is a necessary condition in the Hanafi school. The imam must deliver two separate khutbahs with a sitting in between. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof from the Prophet's practice, and the consequence if the khutbah is omitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the khutbah is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah. Determine what specific act is being ruled upon and its hukm level (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: a hadith from Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's practice, and an athar from Mus'ab ibn Umayr stating the consequence of no khutbah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith indicates the khutbah is integral to Jumu'ah. The description of standing, sitting, then standing again establishes the format and its necessity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Although not explicit in the passage, recognize that other schools differ on the number of khutbahs or the need for a sitting. The Hanafi position is that two khutbahs with a sitting are required.
5
Evaluate the consequence
The athar directly states: if there is no khutbah, one prays four rak'ahs (Zuhr). This shows the khutbah is a condition; its omission invalidates Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣٤٩](٤) ومن شرائطها الخطبة قبل الصلوة يخطب الامام خطبتين يفصل بينهما بقعدة. حديث: عن ابن عمر قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يخطب قائما ثم يقعد ثم يقوم كما يفعلون الآن. واثر: عن مصعب بن عمير قال: وبلغنا انه لا جمعة الا بخطبة فمن لم يخطب صلى اربعا.
And among its conditions is the khutbah before the prayer. The imam delivers two khutbahs, separating them by sitting. Hadith: From Ibn Umar, he said the Prophet would give the khutbah standing, then sit, then stand as they do now. And athar: From Mus'ab ibn Umayr, he said: It has reached us that there is no Jumu'ah except with a khutbah, so whoever does not deliver a khutbah should pray four [rak'ahs].
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage states that the khutbah before the prayer is a condition for Jumu'ah. The imam must deliver two khutbahs with a sitting between them. The proof includes a hadith from Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's practice of standing for the khutbah, sitting, then standing again. Additionally, an athar from Mus'ab ibn Umayr indicates that Jumu'ah is not valid without a khutbah; if omitted, one must pray four rak'ahs of Zuhr instead. The commentary explains that since Jumu'ah has two rak'ahs while Zuhr has four, the two khutbahs substitute for the missing two rak'ahs.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered by the imam before Jumu'ah prayer, consisting of two parts with a sitting in between.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should one do if the imam does not deliver any khutbah before Jumu'ah?
A) The Jumu'ah prayer is still valid
B) One must pray four rak'ahs of Zuhr instead
C) The prayer is invalid but no makeup is needed
D) The imam should be replaced

Key Takeaway
The khutbah is a necessary condition for Jumu'ah; its omission invalidates Jumu'ah and necessitates praying Zuhr.

Khutbah: Standing, Purity, and Minimum Content
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khutbah conditions and minimal content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for the khutbah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding minimal content.

Core Idea
Standing and purity are wajib; minimal dhikr suffices for Abu Hanifa but not for the Sahibayn.

The Friday khutbah is a pillar of Jumu'ah prayer, but what exactly constitutes a valid khutbah? This passage clarifies two undisputed conditions—standing and ritual purity—and then introduces a key disagreement within the Hanafi school: how much speech is needed? Abu Hanifa allows the bare minimum, while his two foremost students demand a proper oration. Understanding this difference sharpens your grasp of how the Hanafi school handles textual evidence and practical authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two uncontested conditions
The text begins by stating the khateeb must deliver the khutbah standing and in a state of ritual purity (wudu). These are the external requirements.
Both conditions are derived from the hadith cited and from analogy with prayer.
2
Locate the point of disagreement
The passage then contrasts Abu Hanifa's position—any dhikr, even minimal, is valid—with the Sahibayn's requirement of a lengthy speech conventionally called a khutbah.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Examine the proofs for standing
The hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah explicitly denies that the Prophet ever gave the khutbah sitting, making standing a necessary practice.
The hadith is sahih and qati' al-thubut, but its dalalah is zanni; hence standing is wajib, not fard.
4
Analyze the evidence for minimal content
Abu Hanifa relies on the athar from al-Sha'bi, which states the Prophet gave the khutbah 'whether little or much.' This supports leniency in content.
The Sahibayn prioritize the general practice of the Prophet's lengthy khutbahs over this solitary report.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi scholars preferred the Sahibayn's view to avoid deviating from established sunnah and to protect the integrity of the khutbah.
The mufta bihi today is that the khutbah must be substantial enough to be called a khutbah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣٥٠](٥) ويخطب قائما على الطهارة فان اقتصر على ذكر الله تعالی جاز عند ابی حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا لا بد من ذكر طويل يسمه خطبة. حديث: عن جابر بن سمرة ان رسول الله كان يخطب قائما ثم يجلس ثم يقوم فيخطب قائما. من حدثك انه كان يخطب جالسا فقد كذب. واثر: عن الشعبي قال يخطب يوم الجمعة ما قل أو كثر.
And he delivers the khutbah standing while in a state of purity. If he confines himself to the remembrance of Allah, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: A lengthy remembrance that is called a khutbah is necessary. Hadith: From Jabir ibn Samurah, the Messenger of Allah would give the khutbah standing, then sit, then stand and give the khutbah standing. Whoever tells you that he used to give the khutbah sitting has lied. Athar: From al-Sha'bi, he said: He would give the khutbah on Friday, whether little or much.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the khutbah. The ruling states that the khutbah should be given standing and with wudu (state of purity). If the imam only utters minimal dhikr (remembrance of Allah), Abu Hanifa considers it sufficient. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require a substantial speech that can be conventionally called a khutbah. The proof for standing is the hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah, which emphatically denies that the Prophet ever gave the khutbah sitting. The athar from al-Sha'bi supports the permissibility of a short khutbah, favouring Abu Hanifa's view. The commentary also notes that while ghusl is better for khutbah, wudu is necessary because the khutbah substitutes for two rak'ahs of prayer requiring purity.

Key Terms
قائما (qa'iman): Standing posture required during the khutbah.
طهارة (taharah): Ritual purity (wudu) required for the khutbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the point of disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the khutbah?
A) Whether standing is required
B) Whether purity is required
C) The minimum length of the khutbah's content
D) Whether sitting between khutbahs is required

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires standing and purity for the khutbah, but there is internal disagreement on content; the mufta bihi requires a substantial speech, not just minimal dhikr.

Khutbah Given Sitting or Without Purity: Valid but Disliked
Ruling on khutbah given sitting or without purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a khutbah delivered sitting or without wudu and distinguish between validity (jawaaz) and dislike (karahah).

Core Idea
A khutbah given sitting or without wudu is valid but makruh — conditions of perfection, not validity.

This short passage addresses a common practical question: what if the imam delivers the Friday khutbah while sitting or without wudu? The author gives a clear ruling: the khutbah is valid (jaza) but disliked (makruh). This distinction between validity and dislike is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh, where many acts are considered valid yet deficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the omitted sunnah
The act is the Jumu'ah khutbah; the omitted practices are standing and purity. These are sunnah acts, not conditions of validity.
Knowing which acts are sunnah versus fard is key.
2
Determine the ruling from the text
The text says 'jaza' (valid) and 'yukrah' (disliked). 'Jaza' means the khutbah fulfills its purpose; 'yukrah' indicates it is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) if without excuse.
Makruh tanzih does not incur sin but is contrary to the preferred practice.
3
Understand the evidence
The previous ahadith and athar emphasized standing and purity, showing they are recommended but not obligatory. Omission does not invalidate.
The evidence is not quoted here but referenced.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some schools consider purity necessary for validity; Hanafis consider it a condition of perfection, not validity.
This affects whether the prayer must be repeated.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the Jumu'ah prayer is valid even if the imam sat or was not in wudu, but it is better to avoid this without excuse.
An excuse removes the dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣٥١](٦) فان خطب قاعدا او على غير طهارة جاز ولكن يكره. ويدل عليه ما تقدم من الاحاديث والاثار الدالة على القيام والطهارة.
If he delivers the khutbah sitting or without purity, it is permissible but disliked (makruh). This is indicated by the previous ahadith and athar that point to standing and purity.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on a khutbah delivered sitting or without wudu. The author clarifies that such a khutbah is still valid in terms of fulfilling the condition for Jumu'ah, but it is makruh (disliked) if done without a valid excuse. The evidence is found in the preceding hadith and athar that require standing and purity; since they indicate what is best, omitting them without necessity is makruh, not invalidating.

Key Terms
جاز (jaza): Permissible/valid in the sense of fulfilling the condition (khutbah is considered given).
يكره (yukrah): Disliked (makruh) – an action that is not sinful but contrary to the preferred practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, an imam delivers the khutbah without wudu. Which of the following is true?
A) The Jumu'ah prayer is invalid because purity is required.
B) The Jumu'ah prayer is valid but the act is disliked.
C) The khutbah must be repeated later.
D) The imam must make up the prayer.

Key Takeaway
A khutbah given sitting or without wudu is valid but disliked if done without excuse; standing and purity are conditions of perfection, not validity.

The Khutbah's Conditions and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Minimal Content
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khutbah minimal content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions of the Friday khutbah and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding minimal content, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A khutbah need not be long—Abu Hanifah allows mere dhikr, but the relied-upon view requires a sermon of reasonable length.

The Friday sermon (khutbah) is a wajib condition for Jumu'ah prayer. In this passage, we learn its basic conditions and a key internal debate: how much content is enough? Imam Abu Hanifah holds that any remembrance of Allah suffices, while his two senior students require a more substantial address. Understanding this difference is crucial for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed conditions
State the conditions that all Hanafis agree on: standing (qiyam) and state of purity (taharah). Also note that the khutbah itself is wajib.
2
Locate the disputed issue
The exact point of difference is the minimal content required for a valid khutbah. Abu Hanifah says any dhikr suffices; the Sahibayn say it must be a lengthy remembrance conventionally called a sermon.
3
Examine Abu Hanifah's position and dalil
Abu Hanifah relies on the hadith of Shu'ayb that the Prophet gave brief words and the athar of al-Sha'bi that the sermon can be little or much. This shows that brevity is permissible.
The essence of the khutbah is dhikr, so minimal dhikr fulfills the requirement.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's position and dalil
The Sahibayn argue that the Prophet's general practice was to give substantial sermons, so the khutbah must be of a length that can be called a sermon.
They consider the customary meaning of 'khutbah' as a speech.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., Al-Marghinani) prefer the Sahibayn's view for caution and conformity with usual practice. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): if someone gives a very short khutbah, according to Abu Hanifah the prayer is valid; according to the mufta bihi, it is not sufficient and the prayer is invalid.
Thus, imams should ensure a sermon of reasonable length.

باب الخطبة [٣٥٠] (٥) ويخطب قائما على الطهارة فان اقتصر على ذكر الله تعالی جاز عند ابی حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا لا بد من ذكر طويل يسمه خطبة [ ٣٥١ (٦) فان خطب قاعدا او شریف ، باب الخطبة قائماص ١٢٥ نمبر ١٩٢٠ مسلم شریف ،فصل يخطب الخطبتين قائما ص ٢٨٣ کتاب الجمعہ نمبر ١/٨٦١ بودا و د شریف، باب الخطبة قائما ص ٦٣ نمبر ١٠٩٤) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو خطبے دیں گے اور دونوں کے درمیان امام بیٹھیں گے۔ اگر خطبہ نہیں پڑھا تو ظہر کی نماز پرھے گا اس کا ثبوت اس اثر میں ہے عن مصعب بن عمير قال و بلغنا انه لا جمعة الا بخطبة فمن لم يخطب صلى اربعا (الف) (سن للبیھقی ، باب وجوب الخطبة وانه اذالم يخطب صلی ظہرا اربعا، ج ثالث ص ٢٧٨، نمبر ٥٧٠٢ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر خطبہ نہیں پڑھا تو ظہر کی چار رکعت پڑھے گا۔ [٣٥٠] (٥) خطبہ دے گا کھڑے ہو کر طہارت پر ، پس اگر صرف ذکر اللہ پر اکتفا کیا تو ابو صنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا لمبا ذکر ضروری ہے جس کو خطبہ کہہ سکے۔
خطبہ کھڑے ہو کر دینے کی دلیل او پر گزرگئی ہے۔ یہ حدیث بھی ہے عن جابر بن سمرة ان رسول الله كان يخطب قائما ثم يجلس ثم يقوم فيخطب قائما . ن حدثك انه كان يخطب جالسا فقد كذب (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الخطبة قائماص ممن . ٦٣ نمبر ١٠٩٣) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خطبہ کھڑے ہو کر دینا چاہئے۔ خطبہ کے لئے غسل بہتر ہے۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں غسل کی تاکید ہے تا ہم وضو ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ خطبہ دورکعت نماز کے بدلے میں ہے اور اس کے بعد فورا نماز پڑھنا ہے اس لئے خطبہ کے لئے وضو ضروری ہے۔ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مختصر سا خطبہ بھی کافی ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے حدثنا شعیب بن رزيق الطائفي ... فقام (رسول الله ) صلى الله متوكـنـا على عصا او قوس فحمد الله واثنى عليه كلمات خفيفات طيبات مباركات (ج) (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الرجل يخطب علی قوس ص ٦٣ نمبر ١٠٩٦) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ کا خطبہ بہت مختصر ہوتا تھا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشعبي قال يخطب يوم الجمعة ما قل أو كثر (و) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب وجوب الخطبة ج ثالث ص ٢٢٢ نمبر ٥٤١٢) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کم خطبہ ہو تب بھی کافی ہو جائے گا۔ نا صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اتنا لمبا خطبہ ہو جس کو خطبہ کہ سکیں۔ اس لئے کہ حضور نے عموما تنالمباخطبہ دیا ہے جس کو خطبہ کہہ سکتے ہیں۔
Chapter of the Sermon. [350] (5) And he delivers the sermon standing, in a state of purity. If he limits it to the remembrance of Allah, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifah, may Allah have mercy on him. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: A lengthy remembrance that can be called a sermon is necessary. [351] (6) If he delivers the sermon sitting or... (references). From this hadith it is understood that there will be two sermons and between them the imam will sit. If he does not deliver the sermon, he prays Zuhr prayer. Its proof is this athar: from Mus'ab ibn Umayr, he said: It has reached us that there is no Jumu'ah except with a sermon; so whoever does not deliver the sermon, prays four (rak'ahs). (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). From this athar it is understood that if he does not deliver the sermon, he prays four rak'ahs of Zuhr. [350] (5) He will deliver the sermon standing with purity. So if he limits it to the remembrance of Allah, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifah, and the two companions said: A lengthy remembrance that can be called a sermon is necessary. The proof for delivering the sermon standing has passed earlier. There is also this hadith: from Jabir ibn Samurah that the Messenger of Allah used to deliver the sermon standing, then sit, then stand and deliver the sermon standing. Whoever tells you that he used to deliver the sermon sitting has lied. (b) (Abu Dawud). From this it is understood that the sermon should be delivered standing. Ghusl is better for the sermon because the hadith emphasizes ghusl, but wudu is necessary because the sermon is in place of two rak'ahs of prayer and prayer immediately follows it, so wudu is necessary for the sermon. According to Abu Hanifah, a very short sermon is sufficient. Its proof is this hadith: Shu'ayb ibn Ruzayq al-Ta'ifi narrated... the Messenger of Allah stood leaning on a staff or bow, praised Allah and extolled Him with light, good, blessed words. (c) (Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is understood that his sermon was very short. (2) There is an athar: from al-Sha'bi, he said: He delivers the sermon on Friday with little or much. (d) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood that even a short sermon suffices. Then the two companions say: The sermon should be lengthy enough to be called a sermon, because the Prophet generally gave a lengthy sermon that can be called a sermon.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minimal content of the Friday sermon (khutbah). The matn states the basic conditions: the khutbah must be delivered standing and in a state of ritual purity. It then presents the difference: according to Imam Abu Hanifah, merely saying 'dhikr Allah' (remembrance of Allah) suffices, while the two companions (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) require a lengthy remembrance that can be conventionally called a sermon. The commentary provides proofs: the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah establishes standing as a sunnah, and the hadith of Shu'ayb shows the Prophet gave brief words. The athar of al-Sha'bi indicates that any amount, little or much, counts as a khutbah. Abu Hanifah's view is based on the idea that the essence of the khutbah is dhikr, so minimal dhikr fulfills it. The Sahibayn argue based on the customary practice of the Prophet, who gave sermons of substantial length. The commentary also notes that wudu is necessary for the khutbah because it substitutes for two rak'ahs of prayer, and the prayer after it requires purity.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Friday prayer, consisting of praise of Allah, blessings on the Prophet, and exhortation.
ذكر الله (dhikr Allah): Any phrase that remembers Allah, such as 'Alhamdulillah' or 'Subhanallah'.
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifah: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school regarding the minimal content of the Friday khutbah?
A) Any remembrance of Allah, no matter how brief, suffices.
B) A lengthy remembrance that can be conventionally called a sermon is necessary.
C) The khutbah must include at least one verse from the Quran.
D) The khutbah must last at least 15 minutes.

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah must be delivered standing and in a state of purity; while Abu Hanifah allowed mere dhikr, the operative Hanafi position requires a sermon of reasonable length.

Ruling on Delivering the Sermon Sitting or Without Purity
States that khutbah is valid but makruh if sitting or without purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delivering the Friday sermon while sitting or without wudu, and explain the evidence and the reason for the dislike.

Core Idea
The khutbah is valid even if sitting or without purity, but it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) because the sunnah is otherwise.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the matn: if the imam delivers the Friday sermon while sitting or without wudu, the sermon remains valid but is considered makruh (disliked). The commentary explains the legal reasoning: the essence of the khutbah is dhikr (remembrance), which does not require standing or purity. However, following the sunnah and the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is superior, so deviating without excuse is disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delivering the Friday sermon (khutbah) while sitting or without wudu. The ruling: jāiz (valid) but makruh tanzihi.
2
Understand the basis for validity
The commentary states the khutbah is essentially dhikr, which does not require standing or purity.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The athar of Mu'awiyah (RA) who sat for one sermon due to old age, indicating permissibility.
Athar in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq
4
Determine why it is makruh
Despite validity, the sunnah is to stand and be in a state of purity because the khutbah is connected to prayer; deviating without excuse is disliked.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is require purity for the khutbah; for them it would be invalid without wudu.

[٣٥١] (٦) فان خطب قاعدا او على غير طهارة جاز ويكره [ ١٣٥٢] (۷) ومن شرائطها الجماعة واقلهم عند ابي حنيفة ثلثة سوى الامام وقالا اثنان سوى الامام [ ٣٥٣] (۸) ويجهر الامام بقرائته في الركعتين وليس فيهما قراءة سورة بعينها [ ۱۳۵۴ (۹) ولا تجب الجمعة على مسافر ولا امرأة ولا ہے اس لئے کہ اصل خطبہ ذکر ہے اور وہ ہو گیا چاہے کھڑے ہو کر ہو یا بیٹھ کر ہو۔ بیٹھ کر خطبہ دینے کا ثبوت اثر میں ہے فلما كان معاوية استأذن الناس فى الجلوس فى احدى الخطبتين وقال انى قد كبرت وقد اردت اجلس احدى الخطبتين فجلس في الخطبة الاولى (الف) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الخطبة قائماج ثالث ص ١٨٨ نمبر ٥٢٦٤) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر خطبہ بیٹھ کر دے تو خطبہ ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح چونکہ خطبہ حقیقت میں نماز نہیں ہے بلکہ ذکر ہے اس لئے بغیر وضو کے خطبہ دے دیا تو خطبہ ہو جائے گا۔ البتہ مکروہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ذکر بغیر وضو کے جائز ہے۔ پہلے احادیث سے ثابت کیا جا چکا ہے۔
[351] (6) If he delivers the sermon sitting or without purity, it is permissible but disliked. [352] (7) Among its conditions is congregation, and the minimum according to Abu Hanifah is three besides the imam, and the two said: two besides the imam. [353] (8) The imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs, and there is no requirement to recite a specific surah. [1354] (9) Jumu'ah is not obligatory on a traveler, nor a woman, nor a sick person, etc. Because the essence of the sermon is remembrance, and that is fulfilled whether done standing or sitting. The proof for delivering the sermon sitting is in the athar: When Mu'awiyah sought permission from the people to sit in one of the two sermons, saying, 'I have grown old and I intend to sit in one of the two sermons,' so he sat in the first sermon. (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood that if he delivers the sermon sitting, the sermon is valid. Similarly, because the sermon is not actually prayer but remembrance, if he delivers the sermon without wudu, the sermon is valid, but it is disliked, because remembrance without wudu is permissible. This has been established by previous hadiths.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of the khutbah when the imam is sitting or not in a state of purity. The matn states that it is permissible (jāz) but disliked (makrūh). The commentary explains: the essence of the khutbah is dhikr (remembrance of Allah), and dhikr is valid whether sitting or standing, with or without wudu. It cites an athar of Mu'awiyah (RA) who, due to old age, sat for the first sermon, and the companions did not object. This indicates that sitting is permissible. However, because the sunnah is to stand (as proven by previous hadiths), sitting without excuse is makrūh tanzīhan. Similarly, since purity is not a condition for dhikr, lacking wudu does not invalidate the khutbah, but it is makrūh because the preferred method is to be in a state of purity, given that the khutbah leads immediately to prayer.

Key Terms
جاز (jāz): Legally permissible; the act fulfills the requirement but may be less than optimal.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an act that is not sinful but goes against the preferred practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam delivers the Friday sermon while sitting, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The khutbah is invalid and Jumu'ah must be repeated
B) The khutbah is valid but it is disliked unless there is an excuse
C) The khutbah is valid and not disliked if he sits once
D) The khutbah is invalid unless he recites Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that the Friday sermon is valid even if the imam sits or lacks wudu, but it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) when done without excuse.

Minimum Congregation for Jumu'ah: Abu Hanifah vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum congregation for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of attendees required for Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn, explain their respective proofs, and apply the ruling to a hypothetical scenario.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires at least three followers per Abu Hanifah, but only two per the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minimum number of participants needed for Jumu'ah prayer. Congregation is a condition (shart) for Friday prayer. The disagreement arises from interpreting a hadith differently. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how the Hanafi school balances textual evidence with analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that congregation is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah; without the minimum number, Jumu'ah is invalid.
2
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifah requires 3 men besides the imam; the Sahibayn require 2 men besides the imam.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Examine the proof
The hadith of Umm Abdullah ad-Dawsiyyah: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory upon the people of every village, even if they are only three, and the fourth is their imam.'
Dar Qutni narration.
4
Analyze the opposing interpretation
The Sahibayn interpret that three total (including imam) suffice, as two followers form a congregation.
Their reasoning: two people constitute a jama'ah in other contexts.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In a town with only three men, Abu Hanifah says Jumu'ah is invalid (pray Zuhr); Sahibayn say it is valid.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifah's view, but the Sahibayn's view may be used in difficulty.

(a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood that if he delivers the sermon sitting, the sermon is valid. Similarly, because the sermon is not actually prayer but remembrance, if he delivers the sermon without wudu, the sermon is valid, but it is disliked, because remembrance without wudu is permissible. [352] (7) Among the conditions of Jumu'ah is congregation, and the minimum according to Abu Hanifah is three men besides the imam, and the two companions say: two men besides the imam. Imam Abu Hanifah's proof is this hadith: from Umm Abdullah ad-Dawsiyyah, she said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory upon the people of every village, even if they are only three, and the fourth is their imam.' (Dar Qutni). From this hadith it is understood that there must be three men besides the imam for Jumu'ah. The two companions said two because two also constitute a congregation, and the third is the imam, so there is a congregation.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum number of participants required for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer. The matn states that this is a condition (shart) of Jumu'ah. Imam Abu Hanifah requires at least three men besides the imam, making four total. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require only two men besides the imam, making three total. The commentary provides Abu Hanifah's proof: a hadith narrated by Umm Abdullah ad-Dawsiyyah, where the Prophet (SAW) states that Jumu'ah is obligatory upon the people of a village even if they are only three, with the fourth being their imam. This indicates that a minimum of four persons (imam + three) are needed. The Sahibayn argue that the word 'three' in the hadith includes the imam (i.e., three total), and that two followers plus an imam constitute a valid congregation. The Hanafi school typically follows Abu Hanifah's view as the stronger one, but some later authorities prefer the Sahibayn due to practical ease.

Key Terms
شرائط الجمعة (shara'it al-jumu'ah): Conditions for the validity of Friday prayer; congregation is one such condition.
جماعت (jama'ah): A group of people praying together; for Jumu'ah, it means at least two or three behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifah (ra), what is the minimum number of attendees (excluding the imam) required for Jumu'ah to be valid?
A) Two men
B) Three men
C) Four men
D) One man

Key Takeaway
The minimum congregation for Jumu'ah in the Hanafi school is three followers according to Abu Hanifah (mufta bihi) and two according to the Sahibayn, both based on the same hadith.

Jahr and Specific Surahs in Jumu'ah
States that imam recites aloud and no specific surah is mandatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jahr in Jumu'ah and explain why reciting specific surahs is mustahabb, not wajib.

Core Idea
Jahr in Jumu'ah is sunnah; no specific surah is obligatory.

In the Friday prayer, the imam leads two rak'ahs with audible recitation. A common question is whether he must recite particular surahs, such as al-Jumu'ah and al-Munafiqun. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: jahr is a confirmed sunnah, and while the Prophet ﷺ often recited those surahs, doing so is recommended, not mandatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine the act under discussion: the imam's recitation in both rak'ahs of Jumu'ah. The ruling is that jahr (loud recitation) is a sunnah muakkadah, and no specific surah is required.
The passage explicitly states: 'The imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs, and there is no requirement to recite a specific surah.'
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proof cited: the hadith of Abu Hurairah, who heard the Prophet ﷺ recite Surah al-Jumu'ah and al-Munafiqun on Friday. This is a sahih hadith (Muslim and Abu Dawud).
The hadith is: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah reciting in them on Friday, i.e., Surah al-Jumu'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith supports the ruling. The Prophet ﷺ recited these specific surahs, but the hadith reports an action (fi'l), not a command (amr). In Hanafi usul, an action indicates istihbab (recommendation) unless it is proven to be obligatory by other evidence. Since no command exists, reciting those surahs is mustahabb.
The absence of an explicit command shifts the ruling from wujub to nadb (recommendation).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (Shafi'i, Hanbali) also view the recitation of these surahs as sunnah, but some may emphasize it more strongly. However, all agree it is not fard. The Hanafi position is that jahr itself is sunnah muakkadah; omitting it is makruh tanzih.
Shafi'is consider reciting Surah al-Jumu'ah and al-Munafiqun as sunnah muakkadah, but not wajib.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that jahr is sunnah, and any surah may be recited. The act of the Prophet is followed as a recommended practice, not an obligation.
This ruling is consistent across Zahir al-Riwayah texts.

[1353] (8) The imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs, and there is no requirement to recite a specific surah. [1354] (9) Jumu'ah is not obligatory on a traveler, nor a woman, nor a sick person, etc. Because the essence of the sermon is remembrance, and that is fulfilled whether done standing or sitting. The proof for delivering the sermon sitting is in the athar: When Mu'awiyah sought permission from the people to sit in one of the two sermons, saying, 'I have grown old and I intend to sit in one of the two sermons,' so he sat in the first sermon. (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood that if he delivers the sermon sitting, the sermon is valid. Similarly, because the sermon is not actually prayer but remembrance, if he delivers the sermon without wudu, the sermon is valid, but it is disliked, because remembrance without wudu is permissible. This has been established by previous hadiths. (1353] (8) The imam will recite aloud in the two rak'ahs. However, reciting a specific surah is not necessary. In a hadith: Marwan appointed Abu Hurairah over Madinah... Abu Hurairah said: I heard the Messenger of Allah reciting in them on Friday, i.e., Surah al-Jumu'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun. (Muslim, Chapter on Recitation of Surah al-Jumu'ah... in Friday Prayer). This hadith indicates that the Prophet recited aloud in both rak'ahs of Jumu'ah. However, reciting those specific surahs is not obligatory, only mustahabb (recommended).

Commentary
This passage states that the imam should recite the Quran aloud (jahr) in both rak'ahs of the Friday prayer. It also clarifies that there is no obligation to recite any particular surah; the commonly recited surahs (e.g., al-Jumu'ah and al-Munafiqun) are mustahabb (recommended) based on the practice of the Prophet. The commentary cites Abu Hurairah's report that he heard the Prophet reciting those two surahs in Jumu'ah. This shows that jahr is the sunnah, but the specific surahs are not fard. The ruling is that any Quranic recitation is valid, as long as it is audible.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Recitation that is audible to others, as opposed to silent (sirr).
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an act that brings reward but is not obligatory.

Who is Exempt from Jumu'ah
Lists those for whom Jumu'ah is not obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six categories of people exempt from Jumu'ah and explain the underlying conditions of obligation.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only wajib on free, adult, male, resident, healthy, sighted Muslims.

Friday prayer is a weekly obligation, but not everyone is required to attend. The Hanafi school lists specific exemptions based on missing conditions of obligation. Understanding these exemptions prevents unnecessary hardship and ensures correct application of the law.

Guided Path
1
List the exemptions
Read the text and list the six categories: traveler (musafir), woman (imra'ah), sick (marid), blind (a'ma), slave ('abd), child (sabi).
Memorize the list as a mnemonic.
2
Identify the missing condition
For each exemption, identify which condition of obligation (shart al-wujub) is absent. e.g., traveler lacks residency, woman lacks maleness, etc.
Conditions: free, adult, male, resident, healthy, sighted.
3
Understand the rationale
Each exemption is based on hardship or inability to fulfill the communal aspect. For example, sick and traveler are excused due to difficulty; blind due to risk; slave and woman due to social roles.
Hanafi fiqh emphasizes ease.
4
Apply to modern scenarios
Think of analogies: e.g., a person with a contagious illness is like the sick; a person in prison may be like a slave in restriction.
The principle of 'absence of condition' remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۵۴] (۹) ولا تجب الجمعة على مسافر ولا امرأة ولا مريض ولا اعمى ولا عبد ولا صبي.
[1354] (9) Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon a traveler, nor a woman, nor a sick person, nor a blind person, nor a slave, nor a child.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling statement listing six categories of people for whom the Friday prayer is not wajib (obligatory): traveler (musafir), woman (imra'ah), sick person (marid), blind person (a'ma), slave (abd), and child (sabi). The commentary (though not present here) would typically explain that these individuals lack the full conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub) such as residency, freedom, sanity, or ability to attend. For women, Jumu'ah is not obligatory but they may attend if they wish. Travelers and sick are exempt due to hardship. Blind and slaves are not required to attend due to inability to fully participate or lack of freedom. Children are exempt until they reach puberty. The list is based on the general principle that Jumu'ah is only obligatory on those who are free, adult, male, resident, healthy, and sighted.

Key Terms
مسافر (musafir): One who intends to travel a distance of three days (approx. 48 miles) and is not a resident.
اعمى (a'ma): A blind person who cannot see; exempted due to inability to safely attend.

Key Takeaway

Minimum Congregation for Jumu'ah: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum congregation for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of participants required for Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, explain their respective proofs, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires at least three besides the imam (Abu Hanifa) or two (Sahibayn); the relied-upon view is three.

One of the conditions for Jumu'ah prayer is the minimum congregation size. Within the Hanafi school, there is an internal dispute between Imām Abū Ḥanīfa and his two leading disciples, Imām Abū Yūsuf and Imām Muḥammad al-Shaybānī. This lesson unpacks both positions, their evidence, and the practical consequence of the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The issue is the minimum number of people required for a valid Jumu'ah congregation, specifically how many besides the imam must be present.
The imam himself is not counted in the minimum.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalīl
Abū Ḥanīfa requires three persons besides the imam. His proof is the ḥadīth of Umm 'Abd Allāh al-Dawsiyya: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory upon the people of every village, even if they are only three and their imam is the fourth.' This text explicitly sets three as the minimum besides the imam.
The ḥadīth is from al-Dāraquṭnī.
3
State the Ṣāḥibayn's position and their dalīl
Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī hold that two persons besides the imam suffice. Their reasoning is that two individuals constitute a congregation (jamā'ah) in other prayers (e.g., fard prayers), and with the imam they become three, so the congregation is established.
They rely on qiyās (analogy) to other congregational prayers.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response and tarjīḥ
The text favours Abū Ḥanīfa by presenting his proof (a clear ḥadīth) and stating that his view is the muftā bihī. The Ṣāḥibayn's analogy is overridden by the explicit textual evidence (al-nass).
In Hanafī uṣūl, a clear text (naṣṣ) takes precedence over analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf
Practically, a Jumu'ah prayer held with only three people total (imam + 2 others) is valid according to the Ṣāḥibayn but invalid according to Abū Ḥanīfa. The muftā bihī follows Abū Ḥanīfa, so such a Jumu'ah must be repeated as Ẓuhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷) ومن شرائطها الجماعة واقلهم عند ابي حنيفة ثلثة سوى الامام وقالا اثنان سوى الامام [۳۵۳]
(۳۵۲] (۷) جمعہ کے شرائط میں سے جماعت ہے اور کم سے کم ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک تین آدمی ہوں امام کے علاوہ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ دو آدمی ہوں امام کے علاوہ۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ام عبد الله الدوسية قالت سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول الجمعة واجبة على اهل كل قرية وان لم يكونوا الا ثلثة ورابعهم امامهم (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب الجمعۃ علی اہل قریہ ج ثانی ص سے نمبر ۱۵۷۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہو کہ امام کے علاوہ تین آدمی ہوں تب جمعہ ہوگا۔
ان صاحبین نے دو آدمی اس لئے کہا کہ دو آدمی بھی جماعت ہوتے ہیں اور تیسرا امام ہے اس لئے جماعت تو ہوگی۔
(7) And among its conditions is congregation (jama'ah), and the minimum according to Abu Hanifa is three besides the imam, and the two (Sahibayn) said two besides the imam [353]. (352) (7) From the conditions of Jumu'ah is congregation, and the minimum according to Abu Hanifa is three men besides the imam, and Sahibayn say two men besides the imam. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is this hadith: from Umm 'Abd Allah al-Dawsiyya that she said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory on the people of every village, even if they are only three and their imam is the fourth.' (b) (Dar Qutni, chapter on Jumu'ah for villagers, vol. 2, page ???, no. 1578). From this hadith it is known that besides the imam there should be three men, then Jumu'ah will be held. The Sahibayn said two men because two men also constitute a congregation, and the third is the imam, so congregation would be established.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minimum number of participants required for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer. The author, following 'Al-Sharh al-Thamiri', begins by quoting the matn: 'Among its conditions is congregation, and the minimum according to Abu Hanifa is three besides the imam, and the two (Sahibayn) said two besides the imam.' The Urdu commentary then elaborates: According to Abu Hanifa, the minimum is three people besides the imam, making a total of four. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that two besides the imam, i.e., a total of three, suffice. Abu Hanifa's proof is the hadith narrated by Umm 'Abd Allah al-Dawsiyya that the Prophet said: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory upon the people of every village, even if they are only three and their imam is the fourth.' This hadith explicitly states that the minimum congregation for Jumu'ah includes three persons besides the imam. The Sahibayn argue that two persons constitute a congregation (jama'ah) in other contexts, and the imam is the third, so the congregation is established. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa, as it is based on a clear hadith and is the foundation of the madhhab.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama'ah): Congregation for prayer. In this context, the minimum number for Jumu'ah.
سوى الإمام (siwa al-imam): Besides the imam, indicating the imam is not counted among the minimum participants.

B) Two

D) Four

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah prayer requires at least three participants besides the imam according to the relied-upon Hanafi position; the Sahibayn's view of two besides imam is not operative for fatwa.

Jahr in Jumu'ah and the Non-Obligation of a Specific Surah
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on reciting aloud in Jumu'ah and explain that no specific surah is obligatory, citing the hadith proof.

Core Idea
In Jumu'ah, loud recitation is sunnah, but no specific surah is required—any surah suffices.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on the imam's recitation during Jumu'ah prayer. While the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited specific surahs, the school holds that loud recitation (jahr) is a confirmed sunnah, but the choice of surah is not restricted. We will examine the hadith evidence and the distinction between obligatory and recommended elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states that the imam recites aloud (jahr) in both rak'ahs. Determine the hukm level of jahr in Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school.
The commentary calls it sunnah; not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The text cites the narration of Abu Hurairah: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah recite Surah al-Jumu'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun on Friday.' Identify its source and transmission.
Hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Understand the distinction between jahr and specific surah
Although the Prophet recited those two surahs, the commentary clarifies that reciting a specific surah is not necessary (ضروری نہیں). Why? Because the hadith shows practice, not command.
The imperative for jahr is derived from continuous practice; for surah, there is no command.
4
Note the mustahab nature
Reciting the surahs the Prophet recited is mustahab (recommended), not wajib. The commentary emphasizes this.
One may recite any surah; the reward is for following the Prophet's example.

Source Text

(8) And the imam recites aloud in the two rak'ahs, and there is no recitation of a specific surah in them [1354]. (1353) (8) The imam will recite aloud in both rak'ahs. However, reciting a specific surah is not necessary. There is a hadith: 'Marwan appointed Abu Hurairah over Madinah... Abu Hurairah said: I heard the Messenger of Allah recite in them on Friday, meaning Surah al-Jumu'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun.' (c) (Muslim, chapter on recitation of Surah al-Jumu'ah... in Salat al-Jumu'ah, p. 287, no. 877; Abu Dawud, chapter on what is recited in Jumu'ah, p. 167, no. 1124). In this hadith it is that I heard these two surahs in the Jumu'ah prayer, meaning that the Prophet used to recite aloud in both rak'ahs of Jumu'ah. Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with its proof regarding the recitation of the imam in Jumu'ah prayer. This is consistent with the Hanafi position that jahr in Jumu'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah.

سورة بعينها (surah bi'aynihi): A specific surah. The text states it is not required to recite a particular surah in Jumu'ah.

Exemptions from Jumu'ah: Categories and Proofs
Ruling listing categories exempted from Jumu'ah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six categories exempt from Jumu'ah and explain the hadith and qiyas basis for each.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is not obligatory on those facing hardship: women, travelers, slaves, sick, boys, and the blind.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on who is exempt from the obligation of Jumu'ah prayer. The source text lists six categories and provides a hadith from Abu Dawud and Dar Qutni as proof. Additionally, the blind and traveler are added by analogy (qiyas) due to the illa of hardship. Understanding these exemptions helps avoid unnecessary burden or misunderstanding about the validity of prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Jumu'ah prayer. The ruling is that it is wajib on free, adult, resident males, but not wajib on the listed categories.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith from Tariq ibn Shihab explicitly exempts four: slave, woman, boy, sick. This is from Abu Dawud and Dar Qutni.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but sufficient for obligation in Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'except' (إلا) definitively lifts the obligation for those four. The ruling is derived from the explicit text.
4
Note the qiyas extension
Traveler and blind are added by qiyas because they share the illa of hardship (haraj) in attending the mosque, similar to the sick.
The illa is extracted by tanqih al-manat: the common factor is genuine difficulty in reaching the congregation.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
The mufta bihi position: Jumu'ah is not obligatory on traveler, woman, sick, boy, slave, or blind. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and agreed upon within the school.

Source Text

(۹) ولا تجب الجمعة على مسافر ولا امرأة ولا مريض ولا صبى ولا عبد ولا اعمی [۳۵۴]
(۱۳۵۴] (۹) جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے مسافر پر، نہ عورت پر ، نہ مریض پر ، نہ بیچے پر، نہ غلام پر ، نہ اندھے پر۔ حدیث میں ہے عن طارق بن شهاب عن النبي الله قال الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة الا اربعة عبد مملوک او امرأة او صبى او مريض (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الجمعة للملوك والمرأة ص ۶۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۷) دار قطنی میں او مسافر کا لفظ بھی ہے (دار قطنی ، باب من تجب علیہ الجمعہ ج ثانی ص ۳ نمبر ۱۵۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مذکورہ لوگوں پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ جمعہ کے لئے بعض مرتبہ دور جانا پڑتا ہے جس کے لئے مذکورہ لوگوں کو جانے میں حرج ہوتا ہے۔ نابینا کو بھی جانے میں حرج ہے اس لئے اس پر بھی جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔

(9) And Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon a traveler, nor a woman, nor a sick person, nor a boy, nor a slave, nor a blind person [354]. (1354) (9) Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon a traveler, nor a woman, nor a sick person, nor a boy, nor a slave, nor a blind person. There is a hadith: from Tariq ibn Shihab from the Prophet, peace be upon him, he said: 'Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation except four: a slave owned, or a woman, or a boy, or a sick person.' (a) (Abu Dawud, chapter on Jumu'ah for slaves and women, p. 60, no. 1067). In Dar Qutni, the word 'traveler' is also added (Dar Qutni, chapter on whom Jumu'ah is obligatory upon, vol. 2, p. 3, no. 1560). From this hadith it is known that Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon the mentioned people. Because for Jumu'ah, sometimes one has to go far, and for these people there is hardship in going. The blind person also has hardship in going, so Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon him either. Footnote: (a) He said: Jumu'ah is obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation except four: slave, woman, boy, and sick person.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that Jumu'ah is not obligatory on certain categories of people. The matn lists: traveler, woman, sick, boy, slave, and blind. The Urdu commentary provides the hadith from Tariq ibn Shihab that the Prophet exempted four: slave, woman, boy, sick. The commentary notes that Dar Qutni includes 'traveler' as well. The blind person is added by analogy due to hardship. The rationale is the hardship (haraj) involved in attending Jumu'ah for these individuals. The hadith is from Abu Dawud, and the blind is included based on the same principle of hardship. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi school's consideration of necessity.

Key Terms
مسافر (musafir): Traveler; one who is on a journey meeting the distance for qasr (approx. 48 miles)
حرج (haraj): Hardship; the reason for exemption from Jumu'ah obligation.
عبد (abd): Slave; a person owned by another.
صبي (sabi): Boy; a male who has not reached puberty.
مريض (marid): Sick person; one who is ill to the extent that attending Jumu'ah would cause hardship.
اعمى (a'ma): Blind person; one who cannot see.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is obligatory on every Muslim except those with a valid excuse; the Hanafi school includes traveler and blind by analogy based on hardship.

Jumu'ah Suffices for Exempted Attendees
Ruling and proof: exempted persons' Jumu'ah suffices for Zuhr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that exempted persons who attend Jumu'ah have their Zuhr obligation fulfilled, and explain the Hanafi proof from the athar.

Core Idea
If an exempted person prays Jumu'ah, it replaces Zuhr — one prayer suffices for the time.

On Friday, certain individuals—such as women, travelers, and the sick—are not obligated to attend Jumu'ah. However, if they do attend and pray with the congregation, a question arises: does this count for their obligatory Zuhr prayer? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that Jumu'ah indeed suffices, supported by reports from al-Hasan al-Basri and al-Zuhri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The source text presents the ruling: if exempted persons attend and pray Jumu'ah with the people, it suffices them for the fard of the time (Zuhr). Identify who is exempted and the exact ruling.
Exempted persons include women, travelers, and the sick.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited consists of two athar: al-Hasan's statement about women, and al-Zuhri's guidance to a traveler. These are considered evidence (dalil) for the ruling.
The athar are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar explicitly indicate that women (who are exempted from Jumu'ah) are sufficed by attending Jumu'ah, and the traveler is encouraged to attend. The Hanafi school uses these to analogize to all exempted categories.
Analogy (qiyas) extends the ruling to all who are not obligated.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
The Hanafi position is considered generally agreed upon (muttafaq alayh); no significant intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute is reported on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۵۵] (۱۰) فان حضروا وصلوا مع الناس اجزاهم عن فرض الوقت
(۱۳۵۵ (۱۰) اگر یہ لوگ حاضر ہوئے اور لوگوں کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی تو ان کو وقتی فرض سے کافی ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح ان لوگوں پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے لیکن اگر ان لوگوں نے جمعہ پڑھ لیا تو ظہران سے ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ جمعہ اگر چہ واجب نہیں ہے لیکن ظہر اور جمعہ میں سے ایک ان پر واجب ہے۔ اس لئے اگر جمعہ پڑھ لیا تو ظہر کے بدلے میں ادا ہو جائے گا۔ یہ اثر ان کی دلیل ہے عن الحسن قال ان جمعن مع الامام اجزاهن من صلوة الامام (ب)(مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ۳۴۰ المرأة تشهد الجمعة اتجزیها صلوۃ الامام ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۱۵۵۶) عن الزهرى قال سألته عن المسافر يمر بقرية فينزل فيها يوم الجمعة قال اذا سمع الاذان فليشهد الجمعة (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب من تجب عليه الجمعة ص۱۷۴ نمبر ۵۲۰۵ ۵۱۷۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ یولوگ جمعہ میں حاضر ہو جائے تو ظہر کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔
[355] (10) And if they attend and pray with the people, it suffices them for the fard of the time. (1355) (10) If these people attend and pray with the people, it will be sufficient for their fard of the time. Explanation: Jumu'ah is not obligatory on these people, but if they do pray Jumu'ah, Zuhr will be dropped from them. Because although Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them, one of Zuhr or Jumu'ah is obligatory on them. So if they pray Jumu'ah, it will be performed as a substitute for Zuhr. The following athar is their proof: from al-Hasan: 'If women pray Jumu'ah with the imam, it suffices them from the imam's prayer.' (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 1556). From al-Zuhri: 'I asked him about a traveler who passes by a village and stays there on Friday. He said: When he hears the adhan, he should attend Jumu'ah.' (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 5205/5173). From this athar it is known that if these people attend Jumu'ah, their Zuhr will be fulfilled.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that exempted individuals who attend Jumu'ah will have it count for their obligatory prayer. The matn states: 'If they attend and pray with the people, it suffices them for the fard of the time.' The commentary explains that Jumu'ah is not wajib on them, but if they pray it, Zuhr becomes waived because one of the two (Zuhr or Jumu'ah) is obligatory on them at that time. The proof comes from athar (reports of the Companions/Tabi'in): al-Hasan al-Basri said that if women pray Jumu'ah with the imam, it suffices them; al-Zuhri said a traveler passing through on Friday should attend Jumu'ah when he hears the adhan. These indicate that these individuals' obligation is fulfilled by attending Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
اجزاهم (ajzāhum): It suffices them; the Jumu'ah prayer fulfills their obligation.
فرض الوقت (fard al-waqt): The obligatory prayer of that time (i.e., Zuhr on Friday).

Key Takeaway
For exempted persons, attending and praying Jumu'ah fulfills the obligation of Zuhr, supported by the practice of the early Muslims.

Who May Lead Jumu'ah: Permissibility of Slaves, Travelers, and the Sick
Ruling that slave, traveler, and sick may lead Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of a slave, traveler, or sick person leading Jumu'ah and identify who is disqualified.

Core Idea
Slaves, travelers, and the sick may lead Jumu'ah because their prayer is valid; women and children may not.

This passage from the matn clarifies that certain individuals exempt from the obligation of Jumu'ah may still serve as imams if they choose to attend. The ruling hinges on the validity of their own prayer and their status as legally responsible (mukallaf). Understanding this expands our view of imamate eligibility beyond the usual assumption that only those obligated can lead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups and their exemption
List the three categories mentioned: slave, traveler, and sick. Note that Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them, but they are mukallaf (sane, adult) and their prayer is valid.
Exemption from obligation does not equal lack of capacity to lead.
2
Understand the basis for permissibility
The commentary explains that imamate requires a valid prayer and being mukallaf. These individuals meet that condition, so their leadership is valid if they choose to attend.
The ruling is based on the general principle of imamate eligibility.
3
Contrast with excluded groups
Women and children are not allowed to lead because they are not generally qualified to lead men in regular prayers. This exclusion applies to Jumu'ah as well.
Women may lead women, but not men in Jumu'ah.

Source Text

(۱۳۵۶ (۱۱) غلام، مسافر اور مریض کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وہ جمعہ میں امامت کرے۔ یہ لوگ عاقل بالغ ہیں اور امامت کے قابل ہیں۔ البتہ ان لوگوں کی سہولت کے لئے ان لوگوں پر جمعہ واجب نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن مشقت برداشت کر کے جمعہ میں آگئے اور جمعہ کی امامت بھی کر لی تو امامت صحیح ہو جائے گی ۔ البتہ عورت اور بچہ عام نمازوں میں امامت کے قابل نہیں ہیں اس لئے جمعہ کی بھی امامت نہیں کر سکتے۔
[356] (11) And it is permissible for the slave, the traveler, and the sick to lead in Jumu'ah. (1356) (11) It is permissible for a slave, traveler, and sick to lead the prayer in Jumu'ah. These people are mature and sane and are capable of leading. However, for their convenience, Jumu'ah is not made obligatory on them. But if they bear the hardship and come to Jumu'ah and also lead the prayer, then their leadership is valid. As for women and children, they are not capable of leading in regular prayers, so they cannot lead in Jumu'ah either.

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling that slave, traveler, and sick are allowed to lead Jumu'ah. The matn states: 'And it is permissible for the slave, the traveler, and the sick to lead in Jumu'ah.' The commentary explains that these individuals are legally responsible (mukallaf) and capable of imamate. The fact that Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them is for their ease, but if they choose to attend and lead, their imamate is valid. In contrast, women and children are not qualified to lead regular prayers, so they cannot lead Jumu'ah either. This ruling is based on the general principle that imamate requires a valid prayer and these individuals qualify.

Key Terms
يؤموا (yu'ammū): They lead in prayer as imam.

Ruling on Praying Zuhr Before Jumu'ah Without Excuse
Ruling that praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is makruh but valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without an excuse and identify the hadith that supports the ruling.

Core Idea
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is valid but makruh — the obligation of Jumu'ah makes it disliked.

This lesson examines a common Friday scenario: what if someone prays Zuhr at home before the imam's Jumu'ah prayer without a valid excuse? The Hanafi school rules that while the Zuhr prayer is valid (jā'iz), the act is makruh (disliked). We will explore the basis for this ruling in the hadith that emphasizes Jumu'ah's obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is praying Zuhr at home before the imam's Jumu'ah prayer without an excuse. The ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) but the prayer is valid.
Note the distinction: the act is disliked, but the prayer is not invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence does the author cite? The hadith of Tariq ibn Shihab that Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation.
The hadith is an ahad hadith, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove that the act is makruh? Jumu'ah is obligatory; praying Zuhr before it shows disregard for that obligation.
The hadith does not explicitly forbid praying Zuhr, but the Hanafi reasoning uses it to establish the dislike.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools hold that Zuhr before Jumu'ah is invalid for those obliged to attend Jumu'ah. The Hanafi school, however, rules that the prayer is still valid.
The practical difference (thamarah) is whether the Zuhr needs to be repeated.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that it is makruh tanzih (disliked, not prohibited) but valid. This is based on the idea that the hadith does not necessitate nullification.
The absence of an explicit prohibition keeps the prayer valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۵۷ (۱۲) ومن صلى الظهر في منزله يام الجمعة قبل صلوة الامام ولا عذر له كره له
(۱۳۵۷) (۱۲) اگر کسی نے جمعہ کے دن امام کی نماز سے پہلے گھر میں ظہر کی نماز پڑھ لی حالانکہ اس کو کوئی عذر نہیں تھا تو یہ اس کے لئے مکروہ ہے۔ لیکن ظہر کی نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔
مکروہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے عن طارق بن شهاب عن النبي الله قال الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة...
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جمعہ ہر مسلمان پر واجب ہے جماعت میں مگر چار آدمی پر غلام ، عورت، بچہ اور بیمار پر
[357] (12) And whoever prays Zuhr in his home on the day of Jumu'ah before the prayer of the imam and he has no excuse, it is makruh for him. (1357) (12) If someone prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the imam's prayer while he has no excuse, then it is makruh for him. But the Zuhr prayer will be valid. The reason for it being makruh is this hadith: from Tariq ibn Shihab from the Prophet, peace be upon him, he said: 'Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation...' Footnote: (a) He said: Jumu'ah is obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation except four: slave, woman, boy, and sick person.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that performing Zuhr at home before the imam's Jumu'ah prayer is makruh (disliked) for someone who has no excuse, but the prayer is still valid (jā'iz). The commentary explains the reason is the hadith which emphasizes the obligation of Jumu'ah on every Muslim without excuse; praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah shows disregard for the obligation. Since the person has no excuse, it is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful enough to invalidate). The Zuhr prayer itself is valid if Jumu'ah is not established or if the person prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse, but the act is disliked.

Key Terms
كره له (kuriha lahu): It is disliked for him; the act is makruh.
عذر (udhr): Excuse; a valid reason for missing Jumu'ah (e.g., travel, sickness).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without a valid excuse is valid (jā'iz) but makruh (disliked) due to the hadith emphasizing Jumu'ah's obligation.

Exemption from Jumu'ah for Sick, Child, Slave, and Traveler
Ruling on exemption and sufficiency of attendance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories exempt from Jumu'ah and explain the ruling if they attend.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is not obligatory on the exempt, but if they attend it suffices for Zuhr.

This passage clarifies a common point: certain individuals are excused from Friday prayer due to hardship, yet if they attend, their prayer is valid and counts for the obligatory Zuhr. The ruling is based on a hadith listing exceptions and supporting athar showing sufficiency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and exempt categories
The text lists who is exempt: sick, child, slave, blind, and traveler (from another narration). Their attendance is optional.
The blind is added by analogy of hardship.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Tariq ibn Shihab states Jumu'ah is wajib on every Muslim in congregation except four: slave, woman, child, sick.
Abu Dawud, Dar Qutni; traveler added elsewhere.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies obligation on others and provides specific exemptions. The athar show that if these categories attend, it suffices instead of Zuhr.
Exemption does not mean their prayer is invalid.
4
Note the consequence of attendance
If they attend Jumu'ah, it fulfills their obligatory Zuhr prayer because one of the two (Zuhr or Jumu'ah) is obligatory on them.
Proof: athar from Hasan and Zuhri in Musannaf works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Sick, nor child, nor slave, nor blind [355] (10) So if they attend and pray with the people, it suffices for them from the obligatory prayer of the time. There is a hadith from Tariq ibn Shihab from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that Jumu'ah is an obligation upon every Muslim in congregation except four: a slave, a woman, a child, or a sick person. (a) (Abu Dawud) In Dar Qutni, the word 'traveler' is also mentioned. From this hadith it is understood that Jumu'ah is not obligatory on the mentioned people. Because sometimes one has to travel far for Jumu'ah, and going would be difficult for these people. The blind also faces difficulty, so Jumu'ah is not obligatory on him either. [355] (10) If these people attend and pray with the people, it will suffice for their present obligation. Explanation: Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them, but if they pray Jumu'ah, it will substitute for Zuhr. Because although Jumu'ah is not obligatory, one of them (Zuhr or Jumu'ah) is obligatory on them. So if they pray Jumu'ah, it will fulfill the obligation instead of Zuhr. This athar is their evidence: from Hasan that if women pray Jumu'ah with the imam, it suffices for them from the prayer of the imam. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) And from Zuhri: he was asked about a traveler who passes through a village and stays there on Friday; he said: if he hears the adhan, he should attend Jumu'ah. (c) (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq) From this athar it is understood that if these people attend Jumu'ah, Zuhr will be fulfilled.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on Jumu'ah exemption and its proof. The author first lists those exempt: the sick, child, slave, blind (and traveler from another narration). Then it explains that if they attend Jumu'ah, it counts for their obligatory Zuhr. The proof is a hadith and two athar. The hadith shows they are exempt, but the athar shows that if they do attend, it is valid. The commentary also notes that the blind is added due to hardship.

Key Terms
جمعة (jum'ah): Friday congregational prayer in the text
معذور (ma'dhur): A person with a valid excuse from an obligation in the context of Jumu'ah exemption

Key Takeaway
