Performing Friday Prayer After the Sermon
Ruling that Friday prayer is performed after the sermon, with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that Friday prayer is performed after the sermon and cite the hadith proof from Anas (RA).

Core Idea
Friday prayer must follow the sermon — the Prophet would attend to needs after the sermon before praying.

In this passage, the author establishes the correct sequence for Friday prayer. The Hanafi school considers the sermon a condition (shart) for Friday prayer, and the prayer must be performed after it. We will examine the hadith evidence from Anas ibn Malik that demonstrates the Prophet's practice, and understand why this order is essential for validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Friday prayer. The ruling (hukm) is that it must be performed after the imam finishes the sermon. The passage explicitly states: 'When the imam finishes his sermon, they establish the prayer.'
The obligation of Friday prayer itself is fard, but this passage focuses on the timing condition.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Anas (RA): 'I saw the Messenger of God not descending from the pulpit when a man would approach him with a need, so he would stand with him until fulfilling his need, then he would stand and pray.' This shows the Prophet prayed after the sermon, not before or during.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Bukhari, though the chain is not given in this text.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's practice of fulfilling needs after the sermon before praying indicates that the sermon is a distinct act that must be completed first. The imperative 'they establish the prayer' after finishing the sermon implies obligation (wujub) of this order.
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation unless specified otherwise.
4
Note the Hanafi position
Hanafis consider the sermon a condition (shart) for Friday prayer. If the prayer is offered before the sermon, it is invalid. The footnote also clarifies that the second adhan is given when the imam sits on the pulpit, before the sermon.
The sermon itself has its own conditions, but this lesson focuses on its timing relative to prayer.
5
Consider the footnote
The footnote from Sa'ib ibn Yazid confirms that the adhan was given in the Prophet's time when he sat on the pulpit, and this practice continued under Abu Bakr and Umar. This reinforces the sequence: adhan, sermon, prayer.
This footnote clarifies that the adhan is a separate recommended act, not a condition.

The footnote clarifies the source. This establishes the sequence: adhan, sermon, then prayer. The Hanafi position is that this order is a condition for the validity of Friday prayer.

اقاموا الصلوة (aqamoo al-salah): They establish the prayer, i.e., stand and begin the congregational prayer.

In Hanafi fiqh, the Friday prayer is valid only if performed after the imam's sermon; the hadith of Anas (RA) proves this sequence.

Hanafi vs Shafi'i: The Legal Status of Eid Prayer
Inter-madhhab dispute on Eid prayer's legal status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Eid prayer, explain the Hanafi proof from Quran and Sunnah, and compare it with the Shafi'i view, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school due to the Prophet's continuous practice; the Shafi'is say it is sunnah.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: are the two Eid prayers obligatory or just recommended? The Hanafis hold it as wajib, while the Shafi'is consider it an emphasized sunnah. Both schools cite Quranic verses and hadith to support their positions. We will walk through the proofs and the practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its core proof
The Hanafis rule that Eid prayer is wajib. Their primary proof is the Quranic commands in Surah al-Baqarah 2:185 and Surah al-Kawthar 108:2, interpreted as referring to the Eid prayer. Additionally, the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri shows the Prophet consistently performing the Eid prayer without ever omitting it, which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (istimrar).
The Hanafi proof is based on both explicit command and continuous practice.
2
Examine the Shafi'i counter-proof
The Shafi'is argue that Eid prayer is only sunnah mu'akkadah, citing the hadith of al-Bara' ibn 'Azib where the Prophet says, 'Whoever does that has attained our sunnah.' The word 'sunnah' is taken to mean a recommended practice, not an obligation.
Shafi'is interpret the word 'sunnah' literally as non-obligatory.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Although not explicitly stated in this passage, the Hanafi response is that the term 'sunnah' in the hadith does not negate obligation; rather, it refers to the Prophet's established practice. The stronger evidence is the Prophet's continuous performance without any break, which, according to Hanafi usul, makes an act wajib.
Istimrar (continuous practice) is a key Hanafi principle in resolving such disputes.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if Eid prayer is wajib, then missing it without a valid excuse incurs sin, and attending the congregation is required for those who are able. If it is sunnah, leaving it is not sinful, though still meritorious.
This difference affects the duty of the individual believer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة العيدين كم ضروری نوں عید کی نماز واجب ہے۔ زمانہ جاہلیت میں لوگ عید مناتے تھے۔ بعد میں اسلام میں بھی اس کو برقرار رکھا۔ اس کا ثبوت اس آیت سے ہے ولتكملوا العدة ولتكبروا الله على ما هداكم ولعلكم تشكرون (الف ) ( آیت ۱۸۵ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) تفسیر طبری میں ہے کہ اس آیت میں عید الفطر میں تکبیر کہنے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اسی آیت کے شروع میں روزے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ جس سے عید الفطر کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے۔ اور فصل لربک وانحر (ب) ( آیت ۲ سورۃ الکوثر ۱۰۸) اس آیت میں تذکرہ ہے کہ پہلے عیدالاضحی کی نماز پڑھو پھر جانور کی قربانی کرو۔ اس لئے دونوں آیتوں سے عید الفطر اور عید الاضحیٰ کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے۔ نماز عیدین کے وجوب کی دلیل اس حدیث کی دلالت ہے عن ابی سعید الخدری قال كان النبي الله يخرج يوم الفطر والأضحى الـى الــمــصـلى فاول شيء يبدأ به الصلوة ثم ينصرف فيقوم مقابل الناس والناس جلوس على صفوفهم فبعثم ويوصيهم ويأمرهم (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الخروج الی المصلی بغیر منبر ص ۱۳۱ نمبر ۹۵۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ ہمیشہ ایسا کرتے تھے کہ عید الفطر و عید الاضحی کے لئے نکلا کرتے تھے، یہ استمرار اور بیشکی وجوب پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔ آپ نے کبھی عیدن کی نماز نہیں چھوڑی یہ وجوب کی دلیل ہے۔ نانه امام شافعی کے نزدیک چونکہ وجوب کا درجہ نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کے یہاں نماز عیدین سنت مؤکدہ ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث بھی ہے عن البراء بن عازب قال قال النبي ال الله ان اول ما يبدأ في يومنا هذا ان نصلى ثم نرجع فنتحر فمن فعل ذلك اصاب سنتنا (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب الخطبة بعد العید ص ۱۳۱ نمبر ۹۶۵) اس حدیث میں اصاب مسنتنا ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عیدین کی نماز سنت ہے۔
Chapter of the two Eid prayers. How much? The Eid prayer is obligatory. In the time of ignorance people celebrated Eid. Later in Islam it was also maintained. Its proof is from this verse: 'That you complete the number and magnify God for what He has guided you, and perhaps you will be grateful' (a) (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185). In Tafsir al-Tabari it is mentioned that this verse refers to saying takbir on Eid al-Fitr, because at the beginning of the verse fasting is mentioned, from which the proof of Eid al-Fitr is established. And 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (b) (Surah al-Kawthar 108:2). This verse mentions that first pray Eid al-Adha prayer and then sacrifice the animal. Therefore both verses establish proof for Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha. The proof of the obligation of Eid prayer is the indication of this hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: The Prophet would go out on the day of Fitr and Adha to the prayer ground, and the first thing he would begin with was the prayer, then he would turn and stand facing the people while they sat in their rows, and he would admonish them, advise them, and command them (c) (Bukhari, chapter of going out to the prayer ground without a pulpit, p. 131, no. 956). This hadith shows that he consistently did this for Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha. This consistency and certainity indicates obligation. He never left the Eid prayer, which is a proof of obligation. But Imam al-Shafi'i does not consider it to have the level of obligation, so according to him the two Eid prayers are emphasized sunnah. Their proof is this hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib: The Prophet said: The first thing we begin on this day is that we pray, then we return and sacrifice. Whoever does that has attained our sunnah (d) (Bukhari, chapter of the sermon after Eid, p. 131, no. 965). In this hadith is 'he has attained our sunnah', from which it is understood that the Eid prayer is sunnah.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the legal status of the two Eid prayers (al-Fitr and al-Adha). The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory). He provides two proofs: 1) Quranic verses—Surah al-Baqarah 2:185 (interpreted to refer to Eid al-Fitr takbir) and Surah al-Kawthar 108:2 (ordering prayer before sacrifice, interpreted as Eid prayer). 2) A hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing the Prophet's consistent practice of leading Eid prayer without ever abandoning it, which indicates obligation (wujub). Then the author presents the Shafi'i position: Eid prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib. Their proof is a hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib where the Prophet says 'he has attained our sunnah,' implying it is sunnah, not obligatory. The text does not provide a Hanafi response, but the earlier proofs are meant to counter this. In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that Eid prayer is wajib (a level below fard but obligatory), and this is the mufta bihi view.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): Legal obligation; an act whose performance is demanded and whose omission incurs sin, based on a zanni proof.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah; an act the Prophet consistently performed and recommended, but not obligatory.
استمرار (istimrar): Continuous practice; the Prophet's consistent action without omission indicates obligation (wujub).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers Eid prayer wajib due to the Prophet's consistent practice; the Shafi'i school views it as sunnah mu'akkadah. The difference stems from how each school interprets the Prophet's actions and the word 'sunnah' in the hadith.

Ruling on Eid Prayer: Obligation or Sunnah
Establishes Hanafi view that Eid prayer is wajib, rebuts Shafi'i claim of sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on Eid prayer, identify the proofs each school uses, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib in Hanafi school, not merely sunnah, based on continuous prophetic practice.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: is Eid prayer obligatory or merely a stressed sunnah? The Hanafi school holds it is wajib, relying on Quranic commands and the Prophet's unwavering practice. The Shafi'i school counters with a hadith that seems to label it as sunnah. Understanding this dispute requires careful attention to how each school interprets terms like 'wajib' and 'sunnah' in their usul frameworks. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate both sides and determine the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its hukm level
Start by clearly stating that the Hanafi school holds Eid prayer to be wajib, not fard. Understand that wajib in Hanafi usul is an obligation with zanni proof, while fard requires qat'i evidence.
Wajib is still obligatory; missing it without excuse is sinful.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil (Quran and hadith)
The passage cites two Quranic verses: al-Baqarah 2:185 (linked to Eid al-Fitr takbir) and al-Kawthar 108:2 (linked to Eid al-Adha prayer and sacrifice). Also, a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing the Prophet always performed Eid prayer first.
The Quranic evidence is indirect (zanni al-dalala), so alone it would not confer fard.
3
Explain why continuous practice indicates wujub in Hanafi usul
In Hanafi usul, continuous practice (istimrar) without any omission by the Prophet is strong evidence for obligation (wujub). The passage argues that the Prophet never left Eid prayer, proving it is not optional.
Istimrar is a form of Sunnah taqririya and indicates that the act was permanently established.
4
State the opposing (Shafi'i) position and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i considers Eid prayer to be sunnah mu'akkadah. Their evidence is a hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib where the Prophet says 'Whoever does that has followed our sunnah' - using 'sunnah' which can mean recommended practice.
The Shafi'i school understands 'sunnah' here in its technical sense of a non-obligatory act.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis believe one must perform Eid prayer, and omitting it without excuse is sinful. Shafi'is consider it a stressed sunnah that one may omit without sin, though it is highly meritorious.
This difference affects fatwa and practice in mixed-madhhab communities.

It is necessary (wajib) to perform Eid prayer. In the time of ignorance, people celebrated Eid. Later in Islam, it was also maintained. Its proof is from this verse: 'And to complete the period and to magnify Allah for having guided you and that perhaps you may be thankful' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185). In Tafsir al-Tabari, it is mentioned that this verse refers to saying takbir on Eid al-Fitr. Because at the beginning of this verse, fasting is mentioned, from which the proof of Eid al-Fitr is derived. And 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (Surah al-Kawthar 108:2). This verse mentions that first perform the Eid al-Adha prayer, then sacrifice the animal. Therefore, both verses prove Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha. The evidence for the obligation of Eid prayer is the indication of this hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: The Prophet ﷺ used to go out on Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha to the prayer place, and the first thing he would begin with was the prayer, then he would turn and stand facing the people while the people were sitting in their rows, and he would admonish them, advise them, and command them. This hadith shows that he always did this; this continuity and unwaveringness indicates obligation. He never left the Eid prayer, which is proof of obligation. As for Imam al-Shafi'i, since according to him it is not of the level of obligation, therefore with him Eid prayer is a stressed sunnah. Their evidence is this hadith: from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib who said: The Prophet ﷺ said: 'The first thing we begin on this day is that we pray, then we return and sacrifice. Whoever does that has followed our sunnah.' In this hadith, 'has followed our sunnah' indicates that Eid prayer is sunnah.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the legal status of Eid prayer. The Hanafi position is that Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory). The author presents two Quranic proofs: (1) The verse from Surah al-Baqarah 2:185, which mentions completing the fast and magnifying Allah; Tafsir al-Tabari links this takbir to Eid al-Fitr. (2) The verse from Surah al-Kawthar 108:2, which commands prayer and sacrifice, interpreted as referring to Eid al-Adha. The author also cites a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing the Prophet's continuous practice (istimrar) of performing Eid prayer, never abandoning it, which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub. The opposing school (Imam al-Shafi'i) argues that Eid prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, relying on a hadith where the Prophet says 'has followed our sunnah' (asaba sunnatana), interpreting the word 'sunnah' as commendable practice rather than obligation. The Hanafi response, implicit in the presentation, is that the continuous practice and specific Quranic commands elevate it to wujub. The passage follows the order: statement of Hanafi view, Quranic evidence, hadith evidence, then the opposing view with its evidence.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujūb): The level of obligation below fard; established by evidence that is zanni al-thubut or zanni al-dalala.
سنت مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A stressed recommended practice that the Prophet consistently performed without making it obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school due to continuous prophetic practice and Quranic commands, distinguishing it from sunnah in Shafi'i school.

Mustahabb Acts Before Eid Prayer: Eating, Ghusl, Perfume, and Best Clothes
Lists and proves recommended acts for Eid day: eating, ghusl, perfume, best clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three mustahabb acts for Eid day and identify the two types of evidence (direct hadith and qiyas to Jumu'ah) used by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Eid sunnahs are established by both direct Prophetic practice and qiyas to Jumu'ah as a congregational gathering.

This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on recommended acts before the Eid prayer. It combines direct hadith evidence for eating and wearing best clothes, and uses qiyas (analogy) to Jumu'ah to derive ghusl, perfume, and fine attire as sunnah. Understanding how the author classifies these acts and proves them will strengthen your ability to trace the derivation of sunnah rulings in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of mustahabb acts
The passage mentions eating before Eid al-Fitr (and after Eid al-Adha), and then ghusl, perfume, and best clothes for both Eids. List them clearly.
Eating is treated separately for Fitr and Adha.
2
Analyze the direct hadith for eating
Examine the hadith from Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet would eat dates (odd number) before Fitr. For Adha, the hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Busr shows he would eat after the sacrifice. Note the difference.
The odd number is a recommended detail.
3
Trace the qiyas argument for ghusl, perfume, and clothes
The author states that Eid is a gathering like Jumu'ah. The hadith for Jumu'ah mentions ghusl, best clothes, and perfume. Since both are congregational gatherings, these acts are transferred to Eid via qiyas.
Identify the asl, far', and illa.
4
Confirm the direct hadith for best clothes
The passage also cites a hadith where 'Umar suggests the Prophet buy a silk garment for Eid and delegations. This directly supports wearing best clothes, independent of the qiyas.
This shows dual evidence for the same act.
5
Determine the hukm level and understand its implications
All these acts are mustahabb (sunnah). They are not obligatory. Omitting them does not invalidate the prayer, but doing them earns reward.
The later toolbox confirms 'sunnah muakkadah'.

(1) On the day of Eid al-Fitr, it is mustahabb for a person to eat something before going out to the prayer place. There is a hadith: from Anas ibn Malik who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ would not go out on Eid al-Fitr until he ate some dates. And in another hadith: he would eat them odd in number. (Bukhari, Book of Eating on Eid al-Fitr before Going Out, no. 953) From the hadith it is understood that one should eat something sweet before going to the prayer place on Eid al-Fitr. And on Eid al-Adha, it is mustahabb to eat after the prayer. The evidence for this is the hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Busr? from his father who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ would not go out on Eid al-Fitr until he had eaten, and he would not eat on the day of Nahr (Adha) until he had sacrificed. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Book of Abandoning Eating on the Day of Nahr until Returning, vol. 3, p. 401, no. 6159)   (2) He should perform ghusl, apply perfume, and wear his best clothes. All these acts are mustahabb on the day of Eid. The evidence for ghusl is the hadith: from Ibn 'Umar that he used to perform ghusl on the two Eids, like a ghusl from janabah. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Book of Ghusl for the Eids, vol. 1, p. 447, no. 1428; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 5772) Because Eid is also a gathering like Jumu'ah, so whatever acts are sunnah in Jumu'ah, the same acts are sunnah in the two Eids. And in Jumu'ah these acts are sunnah, as in the hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Abu Hurayra who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever performs ghusl on Friday, wears from his best clothes, applies perfume if he has it, then comes to Jumu'ah...' (Abu Dawud, Book of Ghusl for Jumu'ah, no. 343) From this hadith it is understood that one should perform ghusl on Friday, wear best clothes, and apply perfume. And since the two Eids are also gatherings like Jumu'ah, these acts become sunnah in them as well. (3) There is a hadith about wearing best clothes on Eid: from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar who said: 'Umar took a garment of silk brocade being sold in the market, brought it to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and said: O Messenger of Allah, buy this and adorn yourself with it for the Eid and the delegations. (Bukhari, Book of What Has Come About the Two Eids and Adorning Oneself in Them, no. 948) In this hadith, 'adorn yourself with it for the Eid and the delegations' indicates that wearing best clothes and beautifying oneself for Eid is sunnah.

Commentary
This passage presents three recommended acts (mustahabb) for Eid day with their evidence. First, on Eid al-Fitr, one should eat something before going to the prayer place, preferably an odd number of dates, following the Prophet's practice. On Eid al-Adha, the recommendation is to eat after the prayer, not before, based on the hadith that the Prophet would not eat until after sacrificing. Second, ghusl, applying perfume, and wearing best clothes are recommended for both Eids. The author uses an analogy (qiyas) with Jumu'ah: since both are large gatherings, the acts that are sunnah for Jumu'ah are also sunnah for Eid. The hadith evidence for Jumu'ah ghusl, perfume, and clothes is cited, then the connection is made. Additionally, a specific hadith about 'Umar advising the Prophet to buy a garment for beautification on Eid provides direct evidence for wearing best clothes. The passage follows the order: each act is stated, then supported by hadith, and the ruling is derived.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustaḥabb): A recommended act; performing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful. Synonymous with sunnah in this context.

Takbir on the Way to Eid Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Presents intra-Hanafi disagreement on reciting takbir loudly while going to Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the loudness of takbir on the way to Eid prayer and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa differentiates between Eids; the Sahibayn say loud for both — the fatwa follows them.

This passage presents a well-known internal disagreement within the Hanafi school: how should one recite takbir while walking to the Eid prayer? Abu Hanifa distinguishes between the two Eids, while his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold a uniform practice. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly applying Hanafi fiqh and recognizing how the school determines its relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the view of Abu Hanifa
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling for each Eid: on Eid al-Fitr, takbir is recited silently; on Eid al-Adha, loudly. Note his reasoning: takbir is a form of du'a, and du'a is better done quietly.
His evidence includes an athar from Ibn 'Abbas.
2
State the view of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that takbir should be recited loudly on the way to both Eids.
The text does not detail their proof, but it likely relies on general practice of the Companions.
3
Identify the mufta bihi position
Within the Hanafi school, the view of the Sahibayn is the relied-upon position for fatwa. This is the operative ruling.
The Zahir al-Riwayah records the Sahibayn's view as the authority.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi following the sunnah may choose either, but the mufta bihi is to recite loudly. Both are valid, but the school prefers the Sahibayn's view.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; neither view is dismissed.

(3) And he proceeds to the prayer place, and he does not recite takbir on the way to the prayer place according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), and he does recite takbir on the way to the prayer place according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. According to Abu Hanifa, on Eid al-Fitr he will not recite takbir loudly on the way, but rather quietly, and on Eid al-Adha he will recite takbir loudly on the way. The reason is that takbir is a type of supplication, and supplication should be recited quietly. Therefore, on Eid al-Fitr he will recite takbir quietly. His (Abu Hanifa's) evidence is this athar: from Shu'bah who said: I was leading Ibn 'Abbas on the day of Eid, and he heard the people reciting takbir. So he said: What is the matter with the people? Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recitation of takbir while going to the Eid prayer place. The matn states: during the journey to the musalla, according to Abu Hanifa, one does not recite takbir (presumably loudly), while according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), one does recite takbir. The commentary clarifies that Abu Hanifa differentiates between the two Eids: on Eid al-Fitr, takbir is recited quietly (sirran) because it is a form of supplication (du'a), and supplication should be humble and quiet; on Eid al-Adha, takbir is recited loudly because of the specific occasion. Abu Hanifa's evidence is an athar from Shu'bah quoting Ibn 'Abbas, who questioned why people were reciting takbir loudly on Eid al-Fitr, implying disapproval. The passage is incomplete as the effect is cut off. The Sahibayn's view is that takbir should be recited loudly on both Eids, perhaps based on general practice. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, i.e., to recite takbir loudly on the way for both Eids.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' (Allah is the Greatest). On Eid, it is recited from the night before until the prayer.
آہستہ (āhista): Quietly, not audible to others. Abu Hanifa holds that on Eid al-Fitr, takbir should be recited silently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on the loudness of takbir on Eid al-Fitr; the mufta bihi is to recite loudly on both Eids.

Eating Before Eid al-Fitr and After Eid al-Adha
Ruling on recommended eating times for Eid prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah regarding eating on Eid days and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Eat before Fitr and after Adha: the Prophet's practice establishes sunnah, not obligation.

This lesson examines the recommended actions of eating on the two Eids. The Hanafi school holds that it is sunnah to eat something sweet before the Eid al-Fitr prayer and to eat after the Eid al-Adha prayer. The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr from Sunan al-Tirmidhi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Note that the passage states two actions: eating before Fitr prayer and eating after Adha prayer. Both are ruled as mustahabb or sunnah.
The ruling is not wajib; it is a recommended practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'كان رسول الله لا يخرج يوم الفطر حتى يطعم ولا يأكل يوم النحر حتى يذبح.' Identify the source: Sunan al-Tirmidhi.
This is an ahad hadith with zanni thubut.
3
Trace wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent practice (لا يخرج حتى يطعم) indicates recommendation. The negation of action before eating shows it was his habit, making it sunnah.
The hadith shows the Prophet's action, which in Hanafi usul indicates sunnah (not fard or wajib) when consistent.
4
Determine the hukm level
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah. It is not wajib because the evidence is zanni al-thubut and the act is not mandated by an imperative.
Sunnah muakkadah means highly recommended; leaving it is not sinful but losing reward.
5
Understand the ikhtilaf
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf_fih: some scholars label it mustahabb, not sunnah, but the Hanafi view treats it as sunnah muakkadah.
In practice, both agree it is not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پہلے عید الفطر میں کچھ میٹھی چیز کھانا چاہئے ۔ اور عیدالاضحیٰ میں نماز کے بعد کھانا مستحب ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله بن بسر عن ابيه قال كان رسول الله لا يخرج يوم الفطر حتى يطعم ولا يأكل يوم النحر حتى يذبح (سنن الترمذي ، باب ترک الاکل یوم النحر حتی مرجع ج ثالث ص ۴۰۱ نمبر ۶۱۵۹ )
Before Eid al-Fitr, one should eat something sweet. And on Eid al-Adha, it is mustahabb to eat after the prayer. Its proof is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Busr from his father, he said: The Messenger of Allah would not go out on the day of Fitr until he ate, and he would not eat on the day of Nahr until he sacrificed.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states the recommended (mustahabb) actions regarding eating on the two Eids. For Eid al-Fitr, it is sunnah to eat something sweet before the prayer, as the Prophet ﷺ would not go out for the prayer until he had eaten. For Eid al-Adha, it is sunnah to eat after the prayer, following the Prophet's practice of not eating until after the sacrifice. The hadith cited is from Sunan al-Tirmidhi and serves as the primary evidence. This ruling is agreed upon in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; equivalent to sunnah in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is mustahabb to eat after the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Eating before Eid al-Fitr and after Eid al-Adha is a confirmed sunnah based on the Prophet's practice, recommended but not obligatory.

Sunan of Eid: Ghusl, Perfume, Best Clothes
Ruling on recommended acts before Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunan acts for Eid, identify their proof from hadith and qiyas, and distinguish them from obligatory acts.

Core Idea
Eid sunan: ghusl, perfume, best clothes — recommended, not obligatory, based on Jumu'ah analogy and hadith.

This passage outlines three recommended acts (sunan) before the Eid prayer: performing ghusl, applying perfume, and wearing one's best clothes. The author provides both direct Prophetic practice and an analogy to Friday (Jumu'ah) as evidence. Understanding these as sunnah (not wajib) is crucial for correct fiqh application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their hukm
Name the three acts: ghusl, tatayyub (perfume), and wearing best clothes. Their hukm is sunnah muakkadah (highly recommended), not fard or wajib.
The phrase 'يغتسل ويتطيب ويلبس احسن ثيابه' clearly lists them.
2
Locate the first proof: direct practice of Ibn Umar
The text cites Ibn Umar's practice of performing ghusl for Eid like ghusl from janabah. This shows the Prophet's companion considered it sunnah.
This is a transmitted practice (athar) used as dalil.
3
Locate the second proof: analogy to Jumu'ah
Eid is a communal gathering like Jumu'ah. The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Abu Huraira establishes ghusl, best clothes, and perfume for Jumu'ah. By qiyas, these acts become sunnah for Eid.
The shared illa (cause) is the communal gathering ('idtimaa').
4
Locate the third proof: specific hadith on beautification for Eid
The hadith of Umar suggesting the Prophet buy a silk cloak for Eid and delegations shows that wearing good clothes for Eid is a recognized practice.
The Prophet did not object, indicating approval (taqrir).
5
Note the hukm level: sunnah not wajib
All proofs indicate recommendation, not obligation. The Hanafi position is that these acts are mustahabb/sunnah muakkadah, based on zanni thubut and the absence of a command with wujub.
Contrast this with acts like the takbirat al-ihram which are fard.

(2) And he performs ghusl, applies perfume, and wears his best clothes. (2) Perform ghusl, apply perfume, and wear good clothes. All these acts are mustahabb on the day of Eid. The proof for ghusl is this hadith: from Ibn Umar that he would perform ghusl on the two Eids like ghusl from janabah. (2) Since Eid is also a gathering like Jumu'ah, whatever is sunnah in Jumu'ah will be sunnah in the two Eids. And in Jumu'ah these acts are sunnah, as in the hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever performs ghusl on Friday, wears his best clothes, and applies perfume if he has it, then comes to the Friday prayer.' This hadith shows that on Friday one should perform ghusl, wear good clothes, and apply perfume; and since the two Eids are also gatherings like Jumu'ah, these acts become sunnah in them. (3) There is a hadith about wearing good clothes on Eid: from Abdullah ibn Umar that Umar took a silk cloak being sold in the market, brought it to the Prophet and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, buy this to adorn yourself with it for Eid and delegations.' This hadith shows that wearing good clothes and beautifying oneself for Eid is sunnah.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, specifically the sunan (recommended acts) for Eid. It states three sunan: ghusl (ritual bath), applying perfume, and wearing one's best clothes. The text provides three proofs: (1) The practice of Ibn Umar who would perform ghusl for Eid like ghusl from janabah, transmitted in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah. (2) An analogy (qiyas) to Jumu'ah, since both are communal gatherings; the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Abu Huraira establishes ghusl, best clothes, and perfume for Jumu'ah, so they apply to Eid by analogy. (3) A specific hadith from Bukhari where Umar suggested the Prophet buy a silk cloak for beautification on Eid and for receiving delegations, indicating that wearing good clothes for Eid is sunnah. The commentary emphasizes that these are sunnah, not obligatory, and are derived from both direct evidence and analogy.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath; a full-body wash with intention, similar to ghusl from janabah.
تطيب (tatayyub): Applying perfume or scent.
احسن ثيابه (ahsan thiyabih): His best clothes; the finest garments one owns.

Takbir on the Way to Eid Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir volume for Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on saying takbir audibly on the way to Eid prayer and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Takbir on the way to Eid is sunnah, but whether loudly on Fitr divides the school.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi disagreement about the volume of takbir when proceeding to the Eid prayer ground. While all agree it is a sunnah act, Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between Eid al-Fitr (quiet) and Eid al-Adha (loud), whereas the Sahibayn hold that it is loud on both occasions. Understanding this dispute reveals how different proofs (athar vs. hadith) lead to different rulings, and which view has become the relied-upon position in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed element
Recognize that the act is saying takbir on the way to the Eid musalla, and the dispute is specifically about the volume — whether it should be said quietly (sirran) or loudly (jahr).
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and its proof
Abu Hanifa holds that on Eid al-Fitr the takbir is said quietly, based on an athar from Ibn Abbas who criticized loud takbir, and the analogy that takbir is a form of supplication which is normally quiet. On Eid al-Adha, he holds it is loud due to many hadith.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that takbir is said loudly on both Eids, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet and Ibn Umar himself would say takbir loudly from home to the musalla on both Eids.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference occurs on Eid al-Fitr: one follows Abu Hanifa by saying quietly or the Sahibayn by saying loudly. The two views are not reconcilable in practice.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., Al-Hidayah) prefer the view of the Sahibayn due to the stronger hadith evidence. The mufta bihi is to say takbir loudly on the way to both Eids.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٣) ويتوجه الى المصلى ولا يكبر في طريق المصلى عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ويكبر فى طريق المصلى عند ابي يوسف و محمد [۳۶۹] (۳) اور عید کی طرف متوجہ ہو۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک راستہ میں تکبیر نہ کہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تکبیر کہے گا عید گاہ کے راستہ میں زور سے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک عید الفطر میں راستہ میں تکبیر زور سے نہیں پڑھے گا بلکہ آہستہ پڑھے گا اور عید الاضحی کے وقت راستہ میں زور سے تکبیر پڑھے گا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ تکبیر ایک قسم کی دعا ہے اور دعا کو آہستہ پڑھنا چاہئے اس لئے عید الفطر میں تکبیر آہستہ پڑھے گا۔ ان کا استدلال اس اثر سے ہے عن شعبة قال كنت اقود ابن عباس يوم العيد فيسمع الناس يكبرون فقال ما شأن الناس قلت يكبرون قال يكبر الامام؟ قلت لا قال امجانين الناس (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ١٣ في التكبير اذا خرج الى العيد ج ثانی ص ۴۸۸، نمبر ۵۶۲۹) اس اثر میں حضرت ابن عباس نے زور سے تکبیر کہنے سے انکار کیا ہے۔ البتہ عید الاضحی میں زور سے تکبیر بہت سی احادیث سے ثابت ہے۔ اس لئے وہاں زور سے تکبیر پڑھے گا۔ فائدہ صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں میں تکبیر زور سے پڑھے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان عبد الله بن عمر اخبره ان رسول الله كان يكبر يوم الفطر من حين يخرج من بيته حتى يأتى المصلى (الف) (دار قطنی ، کتاب العیدین ج ثانی ص ۳۳ نمبر ۱۶۹۸ مستدرک للحاکم ، کتاب صلوۃ العیدین، ج اول ص ۴۳۸، نمبر ۱۱۰۵) (۲) عن ابن عمر انه كان يخرج لعيدين من المسجد فيكبر حتى يأتى المصلى ويكبر حتى يأتى الامام (ب) (دار قطنی، کتاب العیدین ج ثانی ص ۳۳ نمبر ۱۶۹۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید الفطر اور عیدالاضحی دونوں کے راستے میں تکبیر زور سے کہی جائے گی۔
(3) And he heads to the musalla, and he does not say takbir on the way to the musalla according to Abu Hanifa, and he says takbir on the way to the musalla according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. (3) And head towards Eid. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, he should not say takbir loudly on the way; according to the Sahibayn, he will say takbir loudly on the way to the Eidgah. According to Abu Hanifa, on Eid al-Fitr he will not say takbir loudly on the way, but will say it quietly, and on Eid al-Adha he will say takbir loudly on the way. The reason is that takbir is a type of supplication, and supplication should be said quietly, so on Eid al-Fitr he will say takbir quietly. Their evidence is this athar: from Shu'ba: I was leading Ibn Abbas on the day of Eid and he heard the people saying takbir. He said: 'What is the matter with the people?' I said: 'They are saying takbir.' He said: 'Is the imam saying takbir?' I said: 'No.' He said: 'Are the people mad?' In this athar, Ibn Abbas disapproved of saying takbir loudly. However, for Eid al-Adha, saying takbir loudly is established by many hadiths, so there he will say takbir loudly. Benefit: According to the Sahibayn, he will say takbir loudly on both Eids. Their evidence is this hadith: that Abdullah ibn Umar informed him that the Messenger of Allah would say takbir on the day of Fitr from the time he left his house until he reached the musalla. And from Ibn Umar: he would go out for the two Eids from the masjid saying takbir until he reached the musalla, and would continue saying takbir until the imam came. This athar shows that takbir should be said loudly on the way for both Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding saying takbir (Allahu Akbar) audibly on the way to the Eid prayer musalla. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the ruling differs between the two Eids: on Eid al-Fitr, the takbir is said quietly (sirran) because it is a supplication, and he cites an athar from Ibn Abbas who criticized people saying takbir loudly. On Eid al-Adha, due to many hadiths, the takbir is said loudly. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that takbir is said loudly on the way for both Eids, based on the practice of Ibn Umar and the Prophet himself. The text provides proofs for both positions. The dispute is over the nature of takbir: Abu Hanifa sees it as du'a (quiet), while the Sahibayn emphasize public proclamation. The practical difference is whether one says takbir audibly on Eid al-Fitr. The mufta bihi (preferred position) in many later Hanafi works is the view of the Sahibayn, i.e., loud takbir for both, but the text itself does not give a tarjih.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' as a form of glorification; specifically the sunnah takbir on the way to Eid prayer.
مصلى (musalla): The place of prayer, specifically the outdoor prayer ground for Eid (Eidgah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how is the takbir said on the way to Eid al-Fitr?
A) Loudly
B) Quietly
C) Not said at all
D) Only after the prayer

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is saying takbir loudly on the way to both Eid prayers, based on the practice of the Prophet from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Nafl Before Eid Prayer is Makruh, After is Mubah
Ruling on nafl before and after Eid prayer with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl prayers before and after the Eid prayer and explain the proof from the hadith and the reconciling athar.

Core Idea
Nafl before Eid is makruh; after Eid is mubah — the Prophet's practice clarifies the distinction.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling on supererogatory prayers on the day of Eid. The passage presents a hadith that seems to prohibit nafl both before and after the Eid prayer, but then reconciles it with an athar from Ibn Abbas that specifies the dislike is only before the prayer. This distinction is essential for correct practice and understanding how the Hanafi school harmonizes apparent contradictions among primary texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is performing supererogatory (nafl) prayers in the musalla on the day of Eid. The passage states two rulings: (1) No nafl before the Eid prayer, (2) Nafl after is permitted. Determine the precise hukm level for each.
The ruling is not a blanket prohibition but a disliked (makruh) act before, and a permissible (mubah) act after.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The text cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not pray any nafl before or after the Eid prayer. This seems to suggest complete omission. Identify the source and note its transmission.
Hadith from Bukhari and Abu Dawud: the Prophet's action is a proof (dalil) that nafl was not offered.
3
Understand the apparent contradiction
The same narrator (Ibn Abbas) also reported an athar stating that he disliked prayer before the Eid prayer, but did not mention after. This creates a tension: the hadith shows complete omission, while the athar restricts the dislike to before.
The Hanafi method reconciles by treating the athar as a specification (takhsis) of the general implication of the hadith.
4
Apply the Hanafi method of reconciliation
The commentator explains that the Prophet's omission of nafl after may have been due to the fact that he was the imam and left immediately, or because offering nafl after would delay the congregation. The athar from Ibn Abbas explicitly restricts the dislike to before the prayer, implying that after is not disliked.
This follows the usul principle that a specific (khass) text qualifies a general (amm) one.
5
Derive the final ruling
Based on the reconciliation, the Hanafi position is: nafl before the Eid prayer is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful), while nafl after the Eid prayer is permissible (mubah) and not makruh. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that it is makruh to pray nafl before and there is no restriction after.
This ruling applies to both Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٤) ولا يتنفل فى المصلى قبل صلوة العيد ويتنفل بعدها [٣٧٠] (٤) عیدگاہ میں نماز عید سے پہلے نفل نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ اور نفل پڑھی جائے گی نماز عید کے بعد ۔ نفل میں مشغول ہوگا تو عید کی نماز پڑھنے میں دیر ہوگی۔ حالانکہ اس کو سب سے پہلے کرتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس ان النبي الله خرج يوم الفطر فصلى ركعتين لم يصل قبلها ولا بعدها ومعه بلال (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة قبل العيد و بعدهاص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۹۸۹ را بو داؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ بعد صلوۃ العید ص ۷۱ انمبر ۱۱۵۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید کے پہلے اور بعد میں بھی نماز نفل نہیں پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ لیکن دوسرے اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس کرہ الصلوة قبل العيد (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوۃ قبل العيد و بعد ھاص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۹۸۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید سے پہلے تو نفل مکروہ ہے بعد میں نہیں ۔
(4) And he does not perform supererogatory prayer in the musalla before the Eid prayer, and he performs supererogatory prayer after it. (4) In the Eidgah, nafl prayer will not be prayed before the Eid prayer, and nafl will be prayed after the Eid prayer. If he engages in nafl, there will be delay in performing the Eid prayer, although it is prioritized first. (2) There is a hadith: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet went out on the day of Fitr and prayed two rak'ahs; he did not pray before it nor after it, and Bilal was with him. From this hadith it is understood that nafl should not be prayed before or after the Eid prayer. But in another athar, from Ibn Abbas: he disliked prayer before the Eid. From this athar it is understood that nafl before Eid is makruh, not after.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on supererogatory (nafl) prayers in the musalla on the day of Eid. It states that no nafl should be offered before the Eid prayer, but nafl can be offered after it. The text first mentions a hadith where the Prophet did not pray any nafl before or after the Eid prayer, which seems to prohibit nafl both before and after. However, it then cites an athar from Ibn Abbas specifically disliking prayer before the Eid, implying that after the Eid prayer, nafl is permissible. The commentary reconciles the two: the Prophet's action was due to the fact that engaging in nafl before may delay the Eid prayer or give a wrong impression; after the prayer, there is no such concern. Thus, the ruling is: nafl before the Eid prayer is makruh (disliked), while nafl after is permissible (mubah) and not makruh. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
يتنفل (yatanaffal): To perform supererogatory (nafl) prayers.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an act whose omission is better than commission, but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing nafl prayer after the Eid prayer in the musalla?
A) It is makruh.
B) It is permissible (mubah).
C) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes the time for nafl on Eid: disliked before the Eid prayer, permissible after.

Time of Eid Prayer: From Sunrise to Zawal
Ruling on the time window for Eid prayer with prophetic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time window for Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Eid prayer time begins after sunrise (ishraq) and ends at zawal — not at Fajr or sunrise itself.

Understanding the precise time for Eid prayer is important to ensure its validity. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on when the Eid prayer may be performed, based on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr. The passage clarifies that the time is not at sunrise but after the sun has risen sufficiently, and it continues until the sun passes its zenith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Eid prayer, which is sunnah muakkadah. The passage identifies its time as a condition for validity.
Eid prayer is not fard but emphasized sunnah.
2
Locate the time condition
The text states the time starts at irtifa' al-shams (sunrise height) and ends at zawal (midday).
Irtifa' al-shams is about 15-20 minutes after sunrise.
3
Find the proof
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr is cited, where he disapproved of the imam's delay, saying they used to finish by 'the time of tasbih' (ishraq).
This shows the earliest time is after sunrise, not at sunrise.
4
Analyze the dalil
The phrase 'حين التسبيح' indicates the time of ishraq prayer, which is after the sun has risen a spear's length.
This hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud, classified as ahad.
5
Note the practical consequence
Eid prayer should not be performed at Fajr or exactly at sunrise; it should be delayed until after ishraq.
This ensures the time is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥) فاذا حلت الصلوة بارتفاع الشمس دخل وقتها الى الزوال فاذا زالت الشمس خرج وقتها [۳۷۰] (٥) پس جب نماز حلال ہو جائے سورج کے بلند ہونے سے تو نماز عید کا وقت داخل ہو جائے گا زوال تک ، پس جب سورج زائل ہو گیا تو اس کا وقت نکل گیا۔ نماز عید کا وقت سورج تھوڑا اوپر اٹھنے کے بعد سے زوال تک ہے۔ قال خرج عبد الله بن بسر صاحب رسول الله مع الناس في يوم عيد الفطر او اضحی فانکر ابطاء الامام فقال انا كنا قد فرغنا ساعتنا هذه وذلك حين التسبيح (ه) ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب وقت الخروج الی العید ص ۶۸ نمبر ۱۱۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید کی نماز کا وقت صبح صادق سے نہیں بلکہ اشراق کے بعد سے شروع ہوتا ہے۔
(5) So when the prayer becomes permissible by the rising of the sun, its time enters until zawal; when the sun passes its zenith, its time exits. (5) So when prayer becomes permissible due to the sun rising, the time of Eid prayer enters until zawal; when the sun passes its zenith, its time exits. The time of Eid prayer is after the sun rises a little until zawal. He said: Abdullah ibn Busr, a companion of the Messenger of Allah, went out with the people on the day of Eid al-Fitr or al-Adha, and he disapproved of the imam's delay and said: 'We would have finished by this hour, and that was at the time of tasbih (ishraq).' From this hadith it is understood that the time of Eid prayer begins not at Fajr but after Ishraq.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the time of the Eid prayer. It states that the time begins when the sun has risen approximately the height of a spear (i.e., about 15-20 minutes after sunrise, the time of ishraq) and continues until the sun reaches its zenith (zawal). The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr, who said that they would finish the Eid prayer by the time of tasbih (ishraq), indicating that the prayer is performed after sunrise, not at sunrise itself. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the Eid prayer should not be performed too early (at sunrise) nor delayed until after zawal. The optimal time is after ishraq (when the sun has risen sufficiently) until midday.

Key Terms
ارتفاع الشمس (irtifa' al-shams): The sun's rising to a certain height, approximately the length of a spear, marking the time for ishraq prayer and the start of Eid prayer time.
زوال (zawal): The sun's passage of its zenith; the point at which the sun begins to decline in the sky.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) At Fajr
B) At sunrise (shuruq)
C) After the sun has risen (ishraq)

Key Takeaway
The time for Eid prayer begins after sunrise (ishraq) and ends at zawal; it is not valid at sunrise itself.

Voluntary Prayers Before and After Eid: Hanafi Ruling
States ruling and proof for no nawafil before Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers before and after the Eid prayer and derive it from the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer before Eid is makruh; after Eid is permissible — based on the Prophet's action and priority of the Eid prayer.

On the day of Eid, Muslims gather for the special congregational prayer. But what about offering additional voluntary prayers before or after the Eid prayer in the prayer ground? This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and clarifies the reasoning behind the distinction between before and after.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the Arabic matn: 'ولا يتنفل فى المصلى قبل صلوة العيد ويتنفل بعدها'. The ruling is stated: voluntary prayer before Eid is not done; after Eid it is done. The commentary explains the level: makruh before, permissible after.
Note the asymmetry: before is prohibited (makruh), after is allowed.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The text cites a hadith from Ibn Abbas: the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs on Eid and did not pray before or after. This is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sunan Abi Dawud.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but accepted for fiqh rulings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of not praying before or after could imply prohibition. However, a second narration from Ibn Abbas specifically states he disliked prayer before Eid, implying the dislike is before only. The Hanafi school uses this to limit the apparent general prohibition to before.
The commentary resolves the apparent contradiction: the first hadith shows the Prophet's practice; the second clarifies the dislike is before.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
Some scholars allow voluntary prayer before Eid based on the general permissibility of nafl. The Hanafi school prioritizes the evidence of the Prophet's action and the principle of avoiding delay in the Eid prayer.
This is a legitimate difference of opinion (mukhtalaf fih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتنفل فى المصلى قبل صلوة العيد ويتنفل بعدها
[۱۳۶۹ (۴) عیدگاہ میں نماز عید سے پہلے نفل نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ اور نفل پڑھی جائے گی نماز عید کے بعد ۔ نفل میں مشغول ہوگا تو عید کی نماز پڑھنے میں دیر ہوگی۔ حالانکہ اس کو سب سے پہلے کرتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس ان النبى الله خرج يوم الفطر فصلى ركعتين لم يصل قبلها ولا بعدها ومعه بلال (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوة قبل العيد و بعدهاص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۹۸۹ را بو داؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ بعد صلوۃ العید ص ۷۱ انمبر ۱۱۵۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید کے پہلے اور بعد میں بھی نماز نفل نہیں پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ لیکن دوسرے اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس کرہ الصلوة قبل العيد (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلوۃ قبل العيد و بعد ھاص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۹۸۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید سے پہلے تو نفل مکروہ ہے بعد میں نہیں ۔
And he does not perform voluntary prayer in the prayer ground before the Eid prayer, and he performs voluntary prayer after it. [1369 (4) In the Eidgah, voluntary prayer before Eid prayer is not performed. And voluntary prayer will be performed after Eid prayer. If he engages in voluntary prayer, there will be delay in performing the Eid prayer, whereas it [Eid prayer] is done first. (2) There is a hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet (peace be upon him) went out on the day of Fitr and prayed two rak'ahs; he did not pray before it nor after it, and Bilal was with him. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab al-Salah Qabl al-Eid wa Ba'daha, p.135 no.989; Sunan Abi Dawud, Bab al-Salah Ba'd Salah al-Eid, p.71 no.1159) This hadith indicates that one should not pray voluntary prayer before or after Eid. However, in another narration from Ibn Abbas: 'He disliked prayer before Eid.' (Bukhari same reference) This indicates that before Eid it is makruh, but after Eid it is not.]
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling regarding voluntary (nafl) prayer in the musalla on the day of Eid. The Arabic matn states: 'One does not perform voluntary prayer in the musalla before the Eid prayer, and he performs voluntary prayer after it.' The commentary explains that the reason for prohibiting voluntary prayer before Eid is to avoid delay in the Eid prayer, which is given priority. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet did not pray before or after the Eid prayer. However, another effect (athar) from Ibn Abbas specifically indicates dislike (karahah) for prayer before Eid but does not mention after. The Hanafi position, based on these texts, is that voluntary prayer before Eid is makruh, while after Eid it is permissible. The commentary resolves the apparent contradiction by noting that the hadith of no prayer before or after is understood as the Prophet's practice, but the permissibility after is derived from the absence of explicit prohibition in the other narration.

Key Terms
مصلى (musalla): The designated outdoor prayer ground for Eid prayer
تنفل (tanafful): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Disliked but not sinful; better to avoid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that voluntary prayer before Eid is makruh (disliked) to avoid delay, while after Eid it is permissible (mubah), based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the clarifying athar of Ibn Abbas.

Takbir on the Way to Eidgah: Sahibayn's View vs. Abu Hanifa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir for Eids

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding reciting takbir aloud on the way to the Eidgah, identify the Sahibayn's proof from hadith, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Sahibayn: takbir aloud for both Eids; Abu Hanifa: only for Adha.

Reciting takbir on the way to Eid is a sunnah act, but Hanafi imams differ on which Eids it applies to. This passage presents the Sahibayn's evidence for including Eid al-Fitr, based on the practice of Ibn Umar. Understanding this dispute illuminates how the Hanafi school internally weighs different proof sources and sometimes prefers the Sahibayn over Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Recall that Abu Hanifa holds that takbir aloud is only for Eid al-Adha, while the Sahibayn hold it for both Eids. This passage focuses on the Sahibayn's view.
The base matn (not quoted) likely states Abu Hanifa's view.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cite two narrations from Ibn Umar: one that the Prophet ﷺ recited takbir on Fitr, and another that Ibn Umar himself did so for both Eids.
These are hadith of a companion (athar) and a marfu hadith.
3
Understand the istidlal
The Sahibayn use these narrations to argue that the practice of the Prophet and his companion establishes the sunnah for Fitr as well.
The textual operation is expansion probe: expanding the ruling from Adha to Fitr.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: those following Abu Hanifa remain silent on Fitr; those following the Sahibayn recite takbir aloud.
In many Hanafi mosques, the Sahibayn's view is practiced.
5
Assess the tarjih
The passage presents the Sahibayn's evidence favorably, indicating that their view is muftā bihī (operative) or at least acceptable.
Later Hanafi fatwa works (e.g., Radd al-Muhtar) prefer the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدہ صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں میں تکبیر زور سے پڑھے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان عبد الله بن عمر اخبره ان رسول الله كان يكبر يوم الفطر من حين يخرج من بيته حتى يأتى المصلى (الف) (دار قطنی ، کتاب العیدین ج ثانی ص ۳۳ نمبر ۱۶۹۸ مستدرک للحاکم ، کتاب صلوۃ العیدین، ج اول ص ۴۳۸، نمبر ۱۱۰۵) (۲) عن ابن عمر انه كان يخرج لعيدين من المسجد فيكبر حتى يأتى المصلى ويكبر حتى يأتى الامام (ب) (دار قطنی، کتاب العیدین ج ثانی ص ۳۳ نمبر ۱۶۹۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید الفطر اور عیدالاضحی دونوں کے راستے میں تکبیر زور سے کہی جائے گی۔
Benefit: According to the two companions (Sahibayn), for both [Eids] he should recite the takbir aloud. Their proof is this hadith: 'Abdullah ibn Umar informed him that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to recite takbir on the day of Fitr from the time he left his house until he came to the musalla.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Eidain, vol.2 p.33 no.1698; Mustadrak al-Hakim, Kitab Salah al-Eidain, vol.1 p.438 no.1105) (2) From Ibn Umar: 'He used to go out for the two Eids from the mosque and recite takbir until he came to the musalla, and he would continue reciting takbir until the Imam came.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Eidain, vol.2 p.33 no.1696) From this effect, it is understood that on the way to both Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, takbir should be recited aloud.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the recitation of takbir on the way to the Eidgah. The matn (not explicitly quoted) likely states Abu Hanifa's position that takbir is only recited aloud for Eid al-Adha, not for Eid al-Fitr. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, holding that takbir should be recited aloud for both Eids. Their evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar reporting that the Prophet recited takbir on the day of Fitr from his house to the musalla, and another narration that Ibn Umar himself did so for both Eids. The passage concludes that according to this effect, takbir should be recited aloud for both. This is the position of the Sahibayn, and it is likely the mufta bihi (operative) view in later Hanafi practice.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' as a form of remembrance and glorification
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) From his house until the musalla
C) Only inside the musalla
D) Only after the Eid prayer

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's view that takbir is recited for both Eids is the preferred position in the Hanafi school, supported by hadith.

Time of Eid Prayer from Sunrise to Zawal
Defines the time period for performing Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time window for Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school and apply the ruling to determine validity of a given time.

Core Idea
Eid prayer time is strictly from sunrise to zawal; after zawal it is no longer valid.

The Eid prayer is a special congregational prayer with a narrow time window. The Hanafi school defines this window from just after sunrise (the time of ishraq) until the sun reaches its zenith (zawal). The proof comes from the practice of the Companions, as reported in the hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr. Understanding this precise window ensures that the prayer is performed correctly and on time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act under discussion? (Eid prayer) What is its ruling? (wajib) Note the time condition.
The ruling is wajib, but the focus here is on the time condition.
2
Locate the dalil
Read the hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr. What does it indicate about the time of Eid prayer?
The hadith mentions 'saa'atuna hadhihi' and 'hina al-tasbih' (ishraq).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove that the time ends at zawal? Consider the phrase 'when the sun declines, its time exits'.
The companion's statement implies they finished before zawal.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Some allow Eid prayer after zawal. Understand their basis (qiyas on missed prayers).
The Hanafi position is strict; the time is not extendable.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a specific time, determine if Eid prayer is valid. Example: sunrise 6am, zawal 12pm, Eid prayer at 11am is valid; at 1pm is invalid.
If invalid, the congregation must pray Zuhr instead.

So when prayer becomes permissible with the rising of the sun, its time enters until zawal; when the sun declines, its time exits. They say takbir? He said: The Imam says takbir? I said: No. He said: Are the people mad? (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 13, in al-Takbir, from going out to 'Eid, vol.2 p.488 no.5629) In this effect, Ibn Abbas refused to say takbir aloud. However, for Eid al-Adha, saying takbir aloud is proven by many hadith, so there it will be said aloud. Benefit: According to the two companions, for both [Eids] takbir is said aloud. Their proof is this hadith: ... (as earlier). Then: [1370] (5) Then when prayer becomes permissible with the sun's rising, its time enters until zawal; when the sun declines, its time exits. The time of Eid prayer is from when the sun is slightly high until zawal. 'Abdullah ibn Busr, the companion of the Messenger of Allah, went out with the people on the day of Fitr or Adha and objected to the Imam's delay, saying: 'We used to finish at this hour, and that was the time of tasbih (ishraq).' (Abu Dawud, Bab Waqt al-Khuruj ila al-Eid, p.68 no.1135)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the time for Eid prayer. The Arabic matn says: 'When prayer becomes permissible with the rising of the sun, its time enters until zawal; when the sun declines, its time exits.' The commentary explains that the time begins after sunrise (when the sun is high enough, approximately the time of ishraq or duha) and ends at zawal (noon). The proof is the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Busr who said they used to finish the Eid prayer at the time of tasbih (ishraq). The commentary also notes that if the moon for Eid al-Fitr is sighted after zawal, the prayer is not performed that day but the next morning; this is based on a hadith where the Prophet ordered people to fast and go out the next day. Thus, the time for Eid prayer is strictly before zawal.

Key Terms
زوال (zawal): The time when the sun reaches its zenith and begins to decline; noon
ارتفاع الشمس (irtifa' al-shams): The rising of the sun; the time when the sun is well above the horizon (ishraq).
التسبيح (al-tasbih): Literally 'glorification'; here refers to the time of forenoon prayer (salat al-duha or ishraq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the latest time for performing Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sunrise
B) Zawal (noon)
C) Asr
D) Sunset

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer time is strictly from after sunrise (ishraq) until zawal; performing it after zawal invalidates it and it is not made up.

The Number of Rak'ahs in Eid Prayer
Ruling with proof on Eid prayer rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of rak'ahs in Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is exactly two rak'ahs, with no sunnah before or after.

This lesson establishes the essential ruling that the Eid prayer consists of two rak'ahs, as proven by the explicit action of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The passage also clarifies the time for Eid prayer and the absence of any accompanying sunnah prayers. You will learn to identify the key hadith evidence used by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The passage begins by stating that the imam leads the people in two rak'ahs for Eid prayer. This is the core ruling.
The Hanafi school considers this wajib.
2
Identify the primary evidence
The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas (radiyallahu anhuma) is cited: the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed two rak'ahs on the day of Fitr, with no prayer before or after.
This hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Analyze the evidence
The explicit action (fi'l) of the Prophet indicates that the prayer is limited to two rak'ahs. The omission of before/after prayers shows no sunnah is attached.
In Hanafi usul, the action of the Prophet is a proof (sunnah fi'liyyah).
4
Consider the time implications
Two additional hadiths are used to establish the time: Eid prayer is performed after sunrise and before zawal (noon), and if the moon is sighted after zawal, prayer is delayed to the next day.
This reinforces that the two rak'ahs must be performed within that time window.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, when attending Eid prayer, one prays exactly two rak'ahs with the imam, with no additional sunnah prayers before or after at the musalla.
Any individual who misses the congregation prays two rak'ahs similarly.

[۳۷۱ (۶) امام لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے گا دورکعت ۔

[371] (6) The imam leads the people in two rak'ahs. [372] (7) He says takbir in the first rak'ah: takbirat al-ihram... From the hadith it became known that the tasbih, i.e., the Ishraq prayer, the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to finish the Eid prayer at its time. So this is the time of the Eid prayer. (2) In the earlier essential note, a hadith from Bukhari passed, in which were the words: From al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, he said: I heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) delivering a sermon, and he said, 'The first thing we begin with on this day is that we pray, then we return and sacrifice.' (a) (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter on the Two Eids, ... p. 121, no. 95). From this it became known that on this day, the first thing after sunrise is to pray the Eid prayer. Therefore the time of Eid prayer is after the sun has risen, and after zawal the time ends. The proof for this is the hadith: From his uncle among the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that a group of riders came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and testified that they had seen the crescent the previous night, so he ordered them to break their fast and when morning came, to go to their musalla. (b) (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter: If the Imam does not come out for Eid on its day, he comes out the next day, p. 79, no. 1157). In this hadith, they testified seeing the crescent after zawal, so he did not pray that day but told them to pray the next morning. This proves that after zawal the time for Eid does not remain. [371] (6) The imam leads the people in two rak'ahs. In a hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) went out on the day of Fitr and prayed two rak'ahs, not praying before it nor after it. (c) (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: Prayer before and after Eid, p. 135, no. 989). In this hadith, the Prophet only prayed two rak'ahs for Eid. Therefore the Eid prayer is only two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) establishing that the Eid prayer is two rak'ahs led by the imam. The author first cites a hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib indicating that the first act on the day of Eid is prayer, confirming the time after sunrise. Then another hadith from Abu Dawud shows that if the crescent is sighted after zawal (noon), the Eid prayer is postponed to the next day, establishing that the time for Eid ends at zawal. Finally, the primary evidence is from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet prayed exactly two rak'ahs with no before or after sunnah. This is the Hanafi position: Eid prayer is exactly two rak'ahs, and it is not preceded or followed by any sunnah prayer.

Key Terms
ركعتين (rak'atayn): Two units of prayer; the specific number for Eid prayer as performed by the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) Eight rak'ahs
D) One rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is two rak'ahs, and no sunnah prayer is attached to it at the musalla.

Extra Takbirs in Eid Prayer: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on Eid takbir numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number and placement of extra takbirs in Eid prayer and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, including the nature of the difference (istihbab).

Core Idea
The extra takbirs in Eid prayer are sunnah, not wajib; the number differs between schools over istihbab.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling on the extra takbirs (takbir zawā'id) in Eid prayer and the differing view of Imam al-Shafi'i. The passage presents both positions with their proofs, then clarifies that the dispute is over recommendation (istihbab), not obligation. Understanding this highlights how Hanafi fiqh prioritizes certain hadith over others while accommodating valid ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First rak'ah: after takbirat al-ihram, three extra takbirs before recitation. Second rak'ah: after recitation, three extra takbirs before takbir for ruku. Total: four takbirs in each rak'ah including the obligatory ones.
The Hanafi position is based on the hadith of Abu Musa and Hudhayfa and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The proof is a hadith where the Prophet said four takbirs in Eid, and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud for the second rak'ah. These are classified as ahad (zanni thubut), but sufficient for sunnah.
Hanafi usul: sunnah can be established by ahad hadith.
3
State the Shafi'i position and proof
Shafi'i: seven takbirs in first rak'ah, five in second, all before recitation. Their proof is a hadith from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr.
Both proofs are from Sunnah ahad.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text states the difference is over istihbab (recommendation). The Hanafi school does not reject the Shafi'i hadith but considers their own evidence stronger or more appropriate for practice.
Tarjih: Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi congregations say fewer takbirs, while Shafi'i say more. Both are valid sunnah; the prayer remains valid even if the number differs.
This dispute does not affect validity, only preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وثلثا بعدها ثم يقرأ فاتحة الكتاب وسورة معها ثم يكبر تكبيرة يركع بها (۱۳۷۳ (۸) ثم يبدئ في الركعة الثانية بالقراءة فاذا فرغ من القراءة كبر ثلث تكبيرات وكبر تكبيرة رابعة يركع بها [۱۳۷۳ (۹) ويرفع يديه في تكبيرات العيدين.
في الصلوۃ یوم العید ج ثالث ص ۲۹۳ نمبر ۵۶۸۶) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید کی نماز میں پہلی رکعت میں تکبیر احرام کے بعد تین تکبیر کہی جائے گی ۔ تو تکبیر احرام کے ساتھ چار تکبیریں ہو گئیں۔ اس طرح دوسری رکعت میں قرآت کے بعد تین تکبیر زائد کہی جائے گی تو تکبیر رکوع کے ساتھ چار تکبیریں ہو جائیں گی۔ اور دوسری رکعت میں قرآت کے بعد چار تکبیر کہی جائے گی اس کی دلیل بی اثر ہے فاسندوا امرهم الى ابن
مسعود فقال تكبير اربعا قبل القراءة ثم تقرأ فاذا فرغت كبرت فركعت ثم تقوم في الثانية فتقرأ فاذا فرغت كبرت
أربعا (الف) ( سنن سیتی ، باب ذكر الخير الذى روى في التکبیر اربعاج ثالث ص ۴۰۸ نمبر ۶۱۸۳ ) اس اثر میں موجود ہے کہ دوسری رکعت میں قرآت کے بعد چار تکبیر کہی جائے گی۔ تین تکبیر زوائد کی اور ایک تکبیر رکوع کی ہوگی۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک پہلی رکعت میں سات تکبیر اور دوسری رکعت میں پانچ تکبیر کہی جائے گی اور دونوں میں قرآت کے پہلے تکبیر بھی جائے گی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص قال قال نبي الله التكبير في الفطر سبع في الاولى و خمس في الآخرة والقراءة بعدهما كليتهم (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب التكبير فی العیدین ص ۷۰ نمبر ۱۵ار دار قطنی ، کتاب العیدین ج ثانی ص ۳۶ نمبر ۱۷۱۱) ان احادیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ پہلی رکعت میں سات اور دوسری رکعت میں پانچ تکبیریں کہی جائے گی۔ اور قرات سے پہلے کہی جائے گی۔ یہ اختلاف استحباب کا ہے۔
[372] (7) He says takbir in the first rak'ah: takbirat al-ihram, then after it three takbirs, then Surah al-Fatiha and with it a surah, then says takbir and goes into ruku. ... The proof for the three extra takbirs is the hadith: Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman asked how the Messenger of Allah said takbir in al-Adha and al-Fitr. Abu Musa said: He used to say four takbirs like the takbir over the funeral. Hudhayfa said: He spoke the truth. ... From these ahadith it became known that in the Eid prayer, in the first rak'ah after takbirat al-ihram, three takbirs are said. So with takbirat al-ihram there are four takbirs. Similarly in the second rak'ah after recitation, three extra takbirs are said, so with the takbir for ruku there are four takbirs. And the proof for four after recitation in the second rak'ah is the athar: They referred their matter to Ibn Mas'ud, and he said: Say takbir four times before recitation, then recite, then when you finish say takbir and go into ruku, then stand for the second, recite, and when you finish say takbir four times. ... According to Imam al-Shafi'i, in the first rak'ah seven takbirs are said, and in the second rak'ah five takbirs, and in both the takbirs are before recitation. Their proof is the hadith from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr ibn al-'As: The Prophet said: The takbir in al-Fitr is seven in the first and five in the last, and recitation after both. ... This difference is regarding istihbab (recommendation).
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of takbirs in the Eid prayer. The author first presents the Hanafi ruling: in the first rak'ah, after takbirat al-ihram, three extra takbirs are said (making four total including ihram), then recitation, then takbir for ruku. The proof is the hadith of Abu Musa and Hudhayfa where the Prophet said four takbirs in Eid. Then the author mentions the Shafi'i position: seven takbirs in the first rak'ah and five in the second, all before recitation. Their proof is a hadith from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr. The author notes that this difference is regarding recommendation (istihbab), not obligation, implying both practices are valid but the Hanafi is preferred. The Hanafi position is further supported by the athar from Ibn Mas'ud for the second rak'ah.

Key Terms
تکبیر زوائد (takbīr zawā'id): Extra takbirs beyond the obligatory ones (takbirat al-ihram and takbir for ruku) recited in Eid prayer.
استحباب (istihbāb): Recommendation; acts that are encouraged but not obligatory. The author states the difference in number of takbirs is a matter of preference, not obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the extra takbirs in Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) They are wajib, and omission requires sajdah sahw.
B) They are sunnah muakkadah, and omission does not affect validity.
C) They are fard, and omission invalidates the prayer.
D) They are makruh, and saying them is discouraged.

Key Takeaway
The extra takbirs in Eid prayer are sunnah, not fard; the Hanafi school says 3 extra in each rak'ah (different placement), while the Shafi'i school says 7 and 5, and the difference is over istihbab.
