Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Takbirs in the Second Rak'ah of Eid Prayer
Ruling on takbirs in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number and sequence of takbirs in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer and cite the proof from the athar of Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
In the second rak'ah of Eid, four takbirs after recitation: three extra sunnah, one for ruku.

The performance of Eid prayer has specific features that distinguish it from regular prayers. One key feature is the extra takbirs (takbirāt zawā'id). In the second rak'ah, the Hanafi school prescribes a precise sequence after recitation. This lesson unpacks that sequence and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled: the extra takbirs in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer after recitation. The Hanafi ruling is that they are sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
The extra takbirs are separate from the ruku takbir which is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is an athar (report) from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). This is a qawl sahabi, which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
The athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and other collections.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Ibn Mas'ud explicitly instructs: '... in the second (rak'ah) recite, and when you finish, say takbir four times.' The four include three extra and one for ruku. This directly proves the Hanafi sequence.
The phrase 'four times' is clear evidence for the number.
4
Note the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that in the second rak'ah there are five extra takbirs said before recitation, not after. This is a well-known point of difference.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the placement and count of takbirs.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the practice of a prominent Companion, Ibn Mas'ud, and consistent transmission from the early Hanafi imams. This gives the position its authority within the madhhab.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۷۳ (۸) ثم يبدئ في الركعة الثانية بالقراءة فاذا فرغ من القراءة كبر ثلث تكبيرات وكبر تكبيرة رابعة يركع بها [۱۳۷۳ (۹) ويرفع يديه في تكبيرات العيدين.
في الصلوۃ یوم العید ج ثالث ص ۲۹۳ نمبر ۵۶۸۶) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید کی نماز میں پہلی رکعت میں تکبیر احرام کے بعد تین تکبیر کہی جائے گی ۔ تو تکبیر احرام کے ساتھ چار تکبیریں ہو گئیں۔ اس طرح دوسری رکعت میں قرآت کے بعد تین تکبیر زائد کہی جائے گی تو تکبیر رکوع کے ساتھ چار تکبیریں ہو جائیں گی۔ اور دوسری رکعت میں قرآت کے بعد چار تکبیر کہی جائے گی اس کی دلیل بی اثر ہے فاسندوا امرهم الى ابن
مسعود فقال تكبير اربعا قبل القراءة ثم تقرأ فاذا فرغت كبرت فركعت ثم تقوم في الثانية فتقرأ فاذا فرغت كبرت
أربعا (الف) ( سنن سیتی ، باب ذكر الخير الذى روى في التکبیر اربعاج ثالث ص ۴۰۸ نمبر ۶۱۸۳ ) اس اثر میں موجود ہے کہ دوسری رکعت میں قرآت کے بعد چار تکبیر کہی جائے گی۔ تین تکبیر زوائد کی اور ایک تکبیر رکوع کی ہوگی۔
[373] (8) Then he begins the second rak'ah with recitation. When he finishes recitation, he says three takbirs and says a fourth takbir with which he goes into ruku. [374] (9) And he raises his hands in the takbirs of the two Eids. ... From these ahadith it became known that in the Eid prayer, in the first rak'ah after takbirat al-ihram, three takbirs are said. So with takbirat al-ihram there are four takbirs. Similarly in the second rak'ah after recitation, three extra takbirs are said, so with the takbir for ruku there are four takbirs. And the proof for four after recitation in the second rak'ah is the athar: They referred their matter to Ibn Mas'ud, and he said: Say takbir four times before recitation, then recite, then when you finish say takbir and go into ruku, then stand for the second, recite, and when you finish say takbir four times. ... In this athar, it is present that in the second rak'ah after recitation, four takbirs are said: three extra and one takbir for ruku.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling for the second rak'ah of Eid prayer: first recite, then say three extra takbirs, then a fourth takbir to go into ruku. The proof is the athar from Ibn Mas'ud, who instructed to say four takbirs after recitation in the second rak'ah (three extra plus the ruku takbir). This clarifies that the total takbirs in the second rak'ah (excluding takbirat al-ihram) are four, but three are extra (zawa'id) and one is the ruku takbir.

Key Terms
تکبیر رکوع (takbīr al-rukū'): The takbir said when moving into bowing posture; in Eid, it counts as the fourth takbir in the second rak'ah after the three extra ones.
تکبیر زائد (takbīr zā'id): An extra takbir said in Eid prayer beyond the standard takbirs of the prayer; sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many takbirs are said after recitation in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer before going into ruku?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
In the second rak'ah of Eid, say three extra takbirs after recitation, then a fourth takbir for ruku — total four, based on the practice of Ibn Mas'ud.
